كتاب البيوع
وردوسه
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو برای جلد ختم ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کوئی مکیلی چیز کیل کر کے خریدی یا موزونی چیز وزن کر کے خریدی پھر اس کو کیل کیا یا اس کو وزن کیا پھر اس کو کیل کر کے یا وزن کر کے بیچا تو مشتری ثانی کے لیے اس کو پہنایا کھانا جائز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ کیل اور وزن کا اعادہ کر لے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی بیع سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دو پیمانے جاری ہو جائیں ایک پیمانہ بائع کا اور دوسرا مشترکی کا اور اس لیے کر مکیلی اور موزونی چیز مقدار مشروط پر بڑھنے کا احتمال رکھتی ہے اور مقدار زائد بائع کی ہے اور غیر کے مال میں تصرف ( پیونکہ ) حرام ہے اس لیے اس سے بچنا واجب ہے برخلاف اس کے جبکہ اس کو اندازے سے بیچا کیونکہ زیادتی مشتری کے لیے ہے اس لیے کہ ذراع کپڑے میں وصف ہے برخلاف مقدار کے اور بیچ سے پہلے بائع کا نا پنا معتبر نہیں ہے اگر چہ مشتری ثانی کی موجودگی میں ہو کیونکہ یہ بائع یا مشتری کا صاغ نہیں ہے حالانکہ یہی شرط ہے اور عقد بیچ کے بعد بائع کا مشتری کی عدم موجودگی میں ناپنا بھی معتبر نہیں ہے اس لیے کہ کیل کرنا سپرد کرنے کے قبیلہ سے ہے کیونکہ اس کی وجہ سے بیچ معلوم ہو جائے گی اور سپردگی نہیں ہوتی مگر مشتری کی موجودگی میں اور اگر بائع نے عقد بیچ کے بعد مشتری کی موجودگی میں کیل کیا تو کہا گیا کہ ظاہر حدیث کی وجہ سے اس پر اکتفاء نہ کرے کیونکہ دو ناپ کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ اس پر اکتفاء کرے کیونکہ بیج ایک کیل سے معلوم ہوگئی۔ اور سپر ذکرنے کے معنی بھی متحقق ہو گئے اور حدیث کا عمل دو صفتوں کا جمع ہونا ہے۔ چنانچہ ہم باب السلم میں انشاء اللہ ذکر کریں گے اور اگر عددی چیز کو گن کرخریدار تو وہ صاحبین کی روایت کے مطابق مدروع کے مانند ہے کیونکہ یہ مال ربوا نہیں ہے اور ابو حنیفہ کی روایت کے مطابق موزون کے مانند ہے کیونکہ مشتری کے لیے مقدار مشروط پر زیادتی حلال نہیں ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی آدمی نے کوئی مکیلی چیز مثلاً گندم یا جو کیل کرنے کی شرط کے ساتھ خریدی مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں نے سیہ گندم ایک سور و پسیہ کے عوض اس شرط کے ساتھ خریدا کہ یہ دس قفیرز ہیں یا کسی موزونی چیز مثلا لو ہے یا سونے کو وزن کی شرط کے ساتھ خریدا مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں نے ایک سوروپیہ کے عوض یہ لوہا اس شرط کے ساتھ خریدا کہ یہ دس من ہے حاصل یہ کہ مکیلی یا موزونی چیز کو انداز سے سے نہیں خریدا بلکہ کیل یا وزن کی شرط کے ساتھ خریدا پھر مشتری نے اس کو کیل کر کے لے لیا یا اس کو وزن کر کے لے لیا پھر بیع پر قبضہ کرنے کے بعد مشتری نے اس کو بشرط الکیل یا بشرط الوزن فروخت کیا تو مشتری ثانی کو اس بیچ میں تصرف کرنے کی اجازت ہے یہاں تک کہ مشتری ثانی کیل یا وزن کا اعادہ کرے یعنی مشتری ثانی کو کیل یا وزن کرنے سے پہلے بیچ میں تصرف کی اجازت نہیں ہے چنا نچہ وہ نہ اس کو بیچ سکتا ہے اور نہ اس کو کھا سکتا ہے حاصل یہ کہ جس طرح مشتری اول نے اپنے لیے کیل یا وزن کیا تھا اسی طرح مشتری ثانی بھی اپنے لیے کیل یا وزن کرلے یہی قول امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کا ہے۔ دلیل حدیث جابران النبى نهى عن بيع الطعام حتى يجرى فيه صاعان صاع البائع وصاع المشتری ہے۔ یعنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اناج کی بیج سے منع فرمایا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں دوسرتبہ صاع نہ جاری ہو جائے ایک بار بائع کا صاع اور دوسری باز مشتری کا صاع۔ حدیث میں بائع سے مراد مشتری اول ہے اور مشتری سے مراد مشتری ثانی ہے یعنی جب مشتری اول اپنے واسطے کیل یا وزن کر لے تب دوسرے کسی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر سکتا ہے یا اس کو کھا سکتا ہے حدیث کا منشاء یہ بالکل نہیں ہے کہ بیچ واحد میں ایک مرتبہ بائع کیل یا وزن کرے اور دوسری مرتبہ اس کا مشتری کیل یا وزن کمرے کیونکہ اس پر سب کا اتفاق ہے کہ عقد واحد دو مرتبہ کیل یا وزن کا محتاج نہیں ہوتا۔

دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں احتمال ہے کہ شاید وہ مقدار مشروط سے بڑھتی ہو یعنی جب مشتری اول نے کیل یا وزان کر لیا تو شاید اس نے اپنی کیل و وزن میں دھوکا کھایا ہو اور جس قد ربیع مقرر کی ہے اس سے زیادہ ہو اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ زیادتی با کیے جق مشتری اول کا مال ہے اور دوسرے کے مال میں چونکہ تصرف کرنا حرام ہے اس لیے مشتری ثانی کے واسطے اس میں تصرف کرنے سے احتر از واجب ہے اور یہ احتمال اسی وقت دور ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مشتری ثانی خود کیل یا وزن کر کے اطمینان حاصل کر لے۔ اس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری ثانی اپنے بائع یعنی مشتری اول کے کیل یا وزن پر اکتفا نہ کرے بلکہ خود اس کو بھی کیل یا وزن کرنا ضروری ہے ہاں اگر مکیلی یا موزونی چیز کو اندازے سے خریدا تو ناپ تول سے پہلے مشتری کے لیے تصرف کرنا جائز ہے اب اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ ایک شخص نے گندم کی ایک ڈھیری محض اندازے سے ایک سورو پسیہ کے عوض خریدی پھر اس نے دوسرے کو اس اندازے سے فروخت کر دی تو اس صورت میں نہ مشتری اول کو کیل یا وزن کرنے کی ضرورت ہے اور نہ مشتری ثانی کو ضرورت ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں گندم کی ڈھیری کی مقدار متعین کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ڈھیری میں جس قدر گندم ہو گا وہ سب بیع شمار ہوگا۔ اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کیل یا وزن کر کے گندم خریدا مثلاً ایک سورو پسیہ میں دس من گندم خریدا اور مشتری نے وزن کر کے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ پھر محض اندازے سے یہ گندم فروخت کر دیا مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں یہ گندم اس فد رحمن کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو مشتری ثانی اس گندم میں تصرف کے لیے وزن کرنے کا محتاج نہیں ہے بلکہ وزن کرنے سے پہلے اس میں تصرف کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ گندم جس کو دس من سمجھ کر فروخت کیا تھا اگر واقع میں دس من سے زائد ہوا تو یہ زیادتی بھی مشتری ثانی کی ہے اس لیے کہ گندم کی جس ڈھیری کو مشار الیہ بنایا ہے وہ پوری ڈھیری بیج ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری خانی کی ملک ہے تو مشتری خانی اپنی ملک میں تصرف کرنے والا ہوگا ڈھیری میں دس من گندم ہو یا اس سے زائد ہو اور اسی طرح اگر کپڑے کا تھان گڑوں کی شرط کے ساتھ بچا مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں یہ دس گز کا تھان ایک سو روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو نا پنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لیے تصرف کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ ذراع کپڑے کے اندر چونکہ وصف ہوتا ہے اور وصف بیع کے تابع ہوتا ہے اس لیے تھان اگر بجائے دس گز کے بارہ گز کا ہوا تو یہ زیادتی مشتری کے لیے ہوگی نہ کہ بائع کے لیے اور جب زیادتی مشتری کے لئے ہے تو دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنا لازم نہیں آئے گا۔ حالانکہ ناپ تول سے پہلے تصرف کرنا اسی لیے نا جائز تھا کہ ناپ تول سے پہلے تصرف کرنے میں دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنے کا احتمال ہے برخلاف مقدار کے کیونکہ مسیلات اور موزونات میں مقدار وصفہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصل ہوتا ہے اس لیے مکیلی اور موزونی بیج اگر مقدار مشروط سے بڑھ گئی تو وہ زیادتی مشتری کے لے نہ ہوگی بلکہ بائع کے لیے ہوگی پس اگر اس صورت میں کیل یا وزن کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کو تصرف کی اجازت دیدی جائے تو دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنا لازم آئے گا اور یہ نا جائز ہے لیکن اگر کپڑے کا تھان فروخت کیا اور ہر ذراع کا شمن علیحدہ بیان کر دیا مثلا یہ کہا کہ یہ دس گز کا تھان ایک سو روپیہ کے عوض ہے اور ہر گز دس روپیہ کا ہے تو اس صورت میں کپڑا ناپنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لئے تصرف جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہر ذراع کا علیحد شمن ذکر کرنے کی وجہ سے ذراع وصف نہ رہا بلکہ اصل ہو گیا جیسا کہ کتاب البیوع کے شروع میں گذر چکا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بی ثانی سے پہلے بائع یعنی مشتری اول کا کیل کرنا معتبر نہیں ہے۔ اگر چہ اس نے مشتری ثانی کہ موجودگی میں کیل کیا ہو۔ یعنی اس آدمی کی موجودگی میں کیل کیا ہو جو آئندہ مشتری ثانی ہوگا اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حدیث نھی عس
Chapter of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary. And if someone bought a measured item by measuring it, or a weighed item by weighing it, then he measured it or weighed it, and then sold it by measure or weight, it is not permissible for the second buyer to consume it until he repeats the measure or weight. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited the sale of grain until two measures are passed through it: the measure of the seller and the measure of the buyer. And because a measured or weighed item can potentially exceed the stipulated quantity, and the excess belongs to the seller, and disposing of another's property is forbidden, so avoiding this is obligatory. Unlike when it is sold by estimation, because the excess belongs to the buyer, since the yard in cloth is a description, unlike the quantity. And the seller's measurement is not valid before the sale, even if in the presence of the second buyer, because he is not an agent of the seller or buyer, and that is the condition. And the seller's measurement after the contract in the absence of the buyer is also not valid, because measuring is a type of delivery, as the sale becomes known by it, and delivery only occurs in the presence of the buyer. If the seller measured after the contract in the presence of the buyer, it is said that according to the apparent hadith he should not rely on it, because two measures are required, and the correct view is that he should rely on it, because the sale is known by one measure and the meaning of delivery is also realized, and the hadith's operation requires the combination of two qualities. We will mention this in the chapter on salam, God willing. And if a countable item is purchased by counting, then according to the narration of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is like measured cloth (by the yard) because it is not ribawi property, and according to the narration of Abu Hanifa it is like a weighed item because the excess over the stipulated quantity is not lawful for the buyer. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person bought a measured item, e.g., wheat or barley, with the condition of measuring, e.g., he said 'I bought this wheat for one hundred rupees on the condition that it is ten qafiz,' or a weighed item, e.g., iron or gold, with the condition of weighing, e.g., he said 'I bought this iron for one hundred rupees on the condition that it is ten maunds,' meaning he did not buy by estimation but with the condition of measure or weight. Then the buyer measured and took possession, then after possession he sold it with condition of measure or weight. Then the second buyer is not permitted to dispose of it until he repeats the measure or weight; before measuring or weighing he cannot sell or consume it. This is the view of Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad. Evidence: The hadith of Jabir: 'The Prophet forbade the sale of food until two sa' are passed through it: the sa' of the seller and the sa' of the buyer.' The seller in the hadith means the first buyer, and the buyer means the second buyer. The meaning is not that in a single sale the seller measures once and the buyer measures once, as all agree that a single contract does not require two measurements. Second evidence: A measured or weighed item may exceed the stipulated quantity; the first buyer might have made an error in his measure, and the excess belongs to him, and disposing of another's property is forbidden, so the second buyer must avoid it. This possibility is only removed when the second buyer himself measures or weighs. From this evidence it is understood that the second buyer should not rely on the measure of his seller (the first buyer) but must do it himself. However, if the item was bought by estimation, then it is permissible for the buyer to dispose before measure/weight. There are two cases: (1) If a person bought a heap of wheat by estimation for one hundred rupees, then sold it by estimation to another, then neither the first nor second buyer needs to measure/weight, because the quantity is not specified and all wheat in the heap is part of the sale. (2) If a person bought ten maunds of wheat by weight, took possession, then sold it by estimation, e.g., saying 'I sell this wheat for this amount,' then the second buyer does not need to weigh it; he can dispose of it before weighing, because if the heap is more than ten maunds, the excess belongs to the second buyer, as the entire pointed-to heap is owned by him, whether it contains ten or more. Similarly, if a cloth piece is sold with the condition of yards, e.g., 'I sell this ten-yard cloth for one hundred rupees,' it is permissible for the buyer to dispose before measuring, because the yard in cloth is a description, and a description follows the sale; if the cloth is twelve yards, the excess is for the buyer. This is because the prohibition of disposal before measure was due to the possibility of disposing of another's property. Unlike the case of measured/weighed items, where the quantity is not a description but the essence; if the item exceeds the stipulated quantity, the excess belongs to the seller. Thus, if disposal were allowed before measure, it would involve another's property, which is impermissible. However, if the cloth is sold and the price per yard is specified separately, e.g., 'this ten-yard cloth for one hundred rupees, each yard for ten rupees,' then it is not permissible for the buyer to dispose before measuring, because specifying the price per yard makes the yard a core element (asl) rather than a description, as mentioned earlier in the book. The author of Hidayah says: The measurement by the seller (first buyer) is not valid before the second sale, even if he measured in the presence of the second buyer. The reason is the hadith... [cut off]
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya is an expansion (sharh) on a matn from al-Hidayah. It presents the ruling for reselling items that were originally purchased by measure or weight (makyali/mowzuni). The core rule: if a person buys wheat by measuring it, then later sells it to another person with the condition of measure, the second buyer cannot consume or resell it until he measures it himself. The ruling is based on the hadith of Jabir radiyallahu anhu that the Prophet sallallahu alayhi wa sallam forbade selling food until two measures pass through it: one by the first seller and one by the second buyer. The text clarifies that the hadith refers to two separate transactions, not one. The reasoning is that there is a possibility the first buyer's measure was inaccurate, and any excess belongs to the first buyer (now the seller in the second sale). Disposing of it without remeasuring risks consuming someone else's property. However, if the item was sold by estimation (andazah), then no measure is needed because the entire heap is sold and any excess belongs to the second buyer. This is contrasted with cloth sold by the yard: since the yard is a description (wasf), any extra length belongs to the buyer. But if the price per yard is specified separately, the yard becomes a core element and must be measured. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), countable items (ma'dudi) are like cloth (no need for recounting), but according to Imam Abu Hanifa they are like weighed items and must be recounted. The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn. Overall, this passage teaches the importance of precision in transactions to avoid consuming what is not rightfully owned.

Key Terms
عددی (ma'dudi): Items sold by count (e.g. eggs, apples).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what must a second buyer do with countable items (e.g., apples) purchased by count?
A) Recount them before consuming.
B) Consume without recounting.
C) Recount only if the first buyer counted in his presence.
D) Consume only after weighing them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that countable items do not require recounting on resale (Sahibayn's view), and the first buyer's measurement after contract in the second buyer's presence is valid.

The Second Buyer's Duty to Measure
Rational proof for second buyer's duty to measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rational proof (dalil aqli) for why the second buyer must independently measure or weigh goods before disposal, and distinguish when estimation (juzaf) exempts this requirement.

Core Idea
Disposal before measuring is haram because any excess belongs to the first buyer; measurement removes this uncertainty.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a rational argument (dalil aqli) for the Hanafi ruling that the second buyer in a chain of sales must independently confirm quantity before using or reselling the goods. The proof hinges on property rights and the possibility of excess. We will unpack the logic and its exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Determine the exact hukm (legal ruling) for the second buyer regarding measurement before disposal.
The ruling is that the second buyer must measure or weigh himself.
2
Understand the Proof
Analyze the rational argument: any excess over the contracted amount belongs to the first buyer, so disposing before confirmation risks using another's property.
This is a qiyas khafi based on ihtimal (possibility).
3
Note the Exception
When the original sale was by estimation (juzaf), no measurement is required because the entire heap is sold regardless of exact quantity.
Example: a heap of wheat bought by sight, then resold by sight.
4
Apply to a Real Scenario
Consider a modern sale of wheat by weight: the first buyer buys a 100 kg bag, then sells it to a second buyer. The second buyer must re-weigh before using or reselling.
If sold as 'this bag' without specifying weight, estimation applies and no re-weigh needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كتاب البيوع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد هشتم دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کیلی اور وزنی چیز میں احتمال ہے کہ شاید وہ مقدار مشروط سے بڑھتی ہو یعنی جب مشتری اول نے کیل یا وزان کر لیا تو شاید اس نے اپنی کیل و وزن میں دھوکا کھایا ہو اور جس قد ربیع مقرر کی ہے اس سے زیادہ ہو اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ زیادتی با کیے جق مشتری اول کا مال ہے اور دوسرے کے مال میں چونکہ تصرف کرنا حرام ہے اس لیے مشتری ثانی کے واسطے اس میں تصرف کرنے سے
احتر از واجب ہے اور یہ احتمال اسی وقت دور ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مشتری ثانی خود کیل یا وزن کر کے اطمینان حاصل کر لے۔ اس دلیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ مشتری ثانی اپنے بائع یعنی مشتری اول کے کیل یا وزن پر اکتفا نہ کرے بلکہ خود اس کو بھی کیل یا وزن کرنا ضروری ہے ہاں اگر مکیلی یا موزونی چیز کو اندازے سے خریدا تو ناپ تول سے پہلے مشتری کے لیے تصرف کرنا جائز ہے اب اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ ایک شخص نے گندم کی ایک ڈھیری محض اندازے سے ایک سورو پسیہ کے عوض خریدی پھر اس نے دوسرے کو اس اندازے سے فروخت کر دی تو اس صورت میں نہ مشتری اول کو کیل یا وزن کرنے کی ضرورت ہے اور نہ مشتری ثانی کو ضرورت ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں گندم کی ڈھیری کی مقدار متعین کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ڈھیری میں جس قدر گندم ہو گا وہ سب بیع شمار ہوگا۔
Proof. Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 8. The second proof is that in measured and weighed items there is a possibility that it may exceed the contracted amount; that is, when the first buyer measured or weighed, perhaps he made a mistake in his measurement or weighing, and it is more than the amount he fixed. And it is clear that this excess is, by right of contract, the property of the first buyer, and since disposing of another's property is prohibited, it is therefore obligatory for the second buyer to avoid disposing of it, and this possibility can only be removed when the second buyer himself measures or weighs to gain certainty. From this proof it is understood that the second buyer should not rely on the measurement or weighing of his seller (i.e., the first buyer), but it is necessary for him to measure or weigh himself. However, if a measured or weighed item is purchased by estimation, then before measurement/weighing, disposal by the buyer is permissible. There are two scenarios for this: first, a person purchased a heap of wheat purely by estimation for one hundred rupees, then he sold it by estimation to another. In this case, neither the first buyer nor the second buyer needs to measure or weigh, because in this case there is no need to determine the quantity of the heap of wheat; rather, whatever amount of wheat is in the heap, all of it will be considered part of the sale.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof (دليل) for the ruling that the second buyer (مشتری ثانی) must independently measure or weigh goods before disposing of them. The proof is rational: when a measured or weighed item is sold, there is always a possibility that the actual quantity exceeds the contracted amount. Since any excess belongs to the first buyer (بائع/مشتری اول), the second buyer cannot dispose of it without confirming the quantity, as that would involve using another's property without right. Therefore, the second buyer must measure or weigh the goods himself, not relying solely on the first buyer's measurement. The exception: if the original purchase was by estimation (جُزاف, without specifying exact quantity), then the second buyer may dispose of the goods before measuring, because the entire heap is considered sold regardless of its actual amount. The text gives the example of a heap of wheat sold by estimation for a fixed price; in such a sale, no exact quantity is intended, so measuring is unnecessary. This ruling follows the Hanafi school and is based on the principle that uncertainty (احتمال) in quantity must be resolved before disposal to protect property rights.

Key Terms
کیل (kayl): Measurement by volume for dry goods.
وزن (wazn): Measurement by weight.
احتمال (ihtimal): The possibility that actual quantity differs from contracted amount.
مشتری اول (mushtari awwal): The initial buyer who purchases from the original seller.
مشتری ثانی (mushtari thani): The subsequent buyer who purchases from the first buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the second buyer measure or weigh goods himself before disposal?
A) Because the first buyer's measurement is always inaccurate.
B) Because there is a possibility that the actual quantity exceeds the contracted amount, which belongs to the first buyer.
C) Because the hadith requires two separate measurements for every transaction.
D) Because estimation is not permitted in any sale.

Key Takeaway
The second buyer must independently measure or weigh goods sold by measure/weight before disposal; this requirement is lifted if the sale was by estimation.

Two Exceptions to Disposal Before Measurement in Hanafi Sales Law
Explains two specific scenarios where disposal before measurement is allowed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two exceptions where disposal before measurement is permissible and apply the underlying rationale (ʿillah) based on whether quantity is a description (wasf) or essence (asl).

Core Idea
Disposal before measurement is allowed when the quantity is a description, not an essential part.

This passage from Al-Hidayah explores two exceptions to the general rule that a buyer cannot dispose of goods before measuring or weighing. The first exception is when the goods were initially weighed by the first buyer and then sold by estimation (juzāf). The second exception involves cloth sold by the yard with a total fixed price, where the yard is considered a description. Understanding these exceptions requires grasping the distinction between quantity as a description (wasf) and quantity as an essential part (asl), which determines whether the risk of usurping another's property exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the Hanafi rule that a buyer cannot dispose of purchased goods before measuring or weighing them, due to the risk of involving another's property if the actual quantity exceeds the contracted amount.
2
Analyze the first exception (estimated sale)
When the seller initially weighs the goods and then sells them by estimation (juzāf) without specifying exact quantity, the second buyer owns the entire heap as identified. Any excess belongs to the buyer, so disposal before re-weighing is permissible.
The key is that the sale is of the entire heap as a whole, not per unit.
3
Analyze the second exception (cloth with total price)
If cloth is sold with a total price for the whole piece (e.g., 'this ten-yard cloth for one hundred rupees'), the yard is a description (wasf). Any excess in measurement belongs to the buyer, so there is no risk of usurping the seller's property, and disposal before measuring is allowed.
The yard as a description follows the sale.
4
Distinguish the prohibited scenario
For measured/weighed items (makīlāt/mawzūnāt), quantity is an essential part (asl), not a description. If the actual amount exceeds the contracted quantity, the excess belongs to the seller. Thus disposal before measurement would risk usurping the seller's property and is prohibited.
5
Identify the exception's boundary
The cloth exception only applies when the total price is fixed. If the price per yard is specified separately, the yard becomes an essential part (asl), and disposal before measuring is again prohibited.
This distinction demonstrates the principle: when quantity is essential, the prohibition revives.

اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کیل یا وزن کر کے گندم خریدا مثلاً ایک سورو پسیہ میں دس من گندم خریدا اور مشتری نے وزن کر کے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ پھر محض اندازے سے یہ گندم فروخت کر دیا مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں یہ گندم اس فد رحمن کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو مشتری ثانی اس گندم میں تصرف کے لیے وزن کرنے کا محتاج نہیں ہے بلکہ وزن کرنے سے پہلے اس میں تصرف کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ گندم جس کو دس من سمجھ کر فروخت کیا تھا اگر واقع میں دس من سے زائد ہوا تو یہ زیادتی بھی مشتری ثانی کی ہے اس لیے کہ گندم کی جس ڈھیری کو مشار الیہ بنایا ہے وہ پوری ڈھیری بیج ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری خانی کی ملک ہے تو مشتری خانی اپنی ملک میں تصرف کرنے والا ہوگا ڈھیری میں دس من گندم ہو یا اس سے زائد ہو اور اسی طرح اگر کپڑے کا تھان گڑوں کی شرط کے ساتھ بچا مثلا یہ کہا کہ میں یہ دس گز کا تھان ایک سو روپیہ کے عوض فروخت کرتا ہوں تو نا پنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لیے تصرف کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ ذراع کپڑے کے اندر چونکہ وصف ہوتا ہے اور وصف بیع کے تابع ہوتا ہے اس لیے تھان اگر بجائے دس گز کے بارہ گز کا ہوا تو یہ زیادتی مشتری کے لیے ہوگی نہ کہ بائع کے لیے اور جب زیادتی مشتری کے لئے ہے تو دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنا لازم نہیں آئے گا۔ حالانکہ ناپ تول سے پہلے تصرف کرنا اسی لیے نا جائز تھا کہ ناپ تول سے پہلے تصرف کرنے میں دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنے کا احتمال ہے برخلاف مقدار کے کیونکہ مسیلات اور موزونات میں مقدار وصفہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اصل ہوتا ہے اس لیے مکیلی اور موزونی بیج اگر مقدار مشروط سے بڑھ گئی تو وہ زیادتی مشتری کے لے نہ ہوگی بلکہ بائع کے لیے ہوگی پس اگر اس صورت میں کیل یا وزن کرنے سے پہلے مشتری کو تصرف کی اجازت دیدی جائے تو دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کرنا لازم آئے گا اور یہ نا جائز ہے لیکن اگر کپڑے کا تھان فروخت کیا اور ہر ذراع کا شمن علیحدہ بیان کر دیا مثلا یہ کہا کہ یہ دس گز کا تھان ایک سو روپیہ کے عوض ہے اور ہر گز دس روپیہ کا ہے تو اس صورت میں کپڑا ناپنے سے پہلے مشتری کے لئے تصرف جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ ہر ذراع کا علیحد شمن ذکر کرنے کی وجہ سے ذراع وصف نہ رہا بلکہ اصل ہو گیا جیسا کہ کتاب البیوع کے شروع میں گذر چکا ہے۔
And the second scenario is that a person purchased wheat by weight or measure, e.g., he bought ten maunds of wheat for one hundred rupees, and the buyer weighed it and took possession. Then he sold this wheat purely by estimation, e.g., he said, 'I sell this wheat for this amount.' Then the second buyer is not in need of weighing for disposal, but can dispose of it before weighing, because if this wheat, which he sold assuming it to be ten maunds, actually exceeds ten maunds, this excess also belongs to the second buyer, since the heap of wheat that was indicated (as an object of sale) is entirely owned by the second buyer due to the sale, so the second buyer disposes of his own property whether the heap contains ten maunds or more. Similarly, if a cloth piece is sold with the condition of yards, e.g., he said, 'I sell this ten-yard cloth piece for one hundred rupees,' then before measuring, it is permissible for the buyer to dispose of it, because the yard is a description within the cloth, and the description follows the sale. So if the cloth turns out to be twelve yards instead of ten, this excess is for the buyer, not for the seller. And when the excess is for the buyer, then disposing of another's property does not become necessary. However, disposal before measurement and weighing was impermissible only because there is a possibility of disposing of another's property. This is in contrast to quantity, because in measured and weighed items, quantity is not a description but the essence. Therefore, if a measured or weighed sale exceeds the contracted amount, that excess will not be for the buyer but for the seller. So if in this case the buyer were allowed to dispose before measuring or weighing, it would necessitate disposing of another's property, and that is impermissible. But if a cloth piece is sold and the price of each yard is mentioned separately, e.g., he said, 'This ten-yard cloth is for one hundred rupees, and each yard is ten rupees,' then in this case, it is not permissible for the buyer to dispose before measuring, because mentioning the price of each yard separately makes the yard not a description but an essential part, as has passed earlier in the Book of Sales.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage discusses two exceptional scenarios where disposal before measurement is permitted. The first: when the first buyer weighs the goods and then sells them by estimation (جزاف) without specifying exact quantity. In this case, the second buyer may dispose without re-weighing because the entire heap, regardless of actual weight, belongs to him. The reason is that the sale was by estimation, so any excess or deficiency is absorbed into the sale; the second buyer owns the entire heap as identified. The second scenario: cloth sold by the yard with a total price (e.g., ten yards for one hundred rupees). Here, the yard is considered a description (وصف) of the cloth, and if the actual measurement differs, the excess belongs to the buyer, so no fear of usurping the seller's property. However, if the price per yard is separately fixed, then the yard becomes an essential part (اصل), and the same rule as for measured goods applies: disposal before measurement is not allowed. This distinction highlights the Hanafi principle that when quantity is a mere description, the risk of usurpation is absent. The passage reinforces the general rule by explaining the underlying rationale (علت): the prohibition of disposal before measurement is due to the possibility of involving another's property; when that possibility is removed (as in estimated or description-based sales), the prohibition lifts.

Key Terms
جزاف (juzāf): Sale by estimation without specifying exact quantity or measurement.
وصف (wasf): An attribute or description of an item, such as the yard measurement in cloth when the total price is set.
اصل (asl): The essential, quantified component of an item, such as when each unit price is separately specified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario can the buyer dispose of a cloth piece before measuring?
A) When the price per yard is mentioned separately.
B) When the total price is mentioned for the entire cloth piece.
C) When the cloth is sold by weight.
D) When the cloth is sold by estimation.

Key Takeaway
Disposal before measurement is permissible when the sale is by estimation (juzāf) or when the yard is a description (wasf) in cloth, but prohibited when quantity is an essential part (asl).

Measurement by a Non-Party is Invalid
Ruling on measurement by a non-party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a seller's measurement before the contract is invalid for the buyer and explain the rationale based on the hadith and the condition of delivery.

Core Idea
Measurement is only valid if done by the actual buyer or seller after the contract is formed.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from Al-Hidayah: the measurement done by the first buyer (who later becomes the seller) is not valid for the second buyer, even if the second buyer was present during the measurement. The reasoning ties directly to the hadith requiring possession (including measurement) by the actual parties and the condition that delivery must occur in the buyer's presence. Understanding this clarifies the importance of the proper timing and parties in sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage explicitly states that the measurement by the seller (first buyer) is not acceptable (معتبر نہیں) for the second buyer, even if done in the second buyer's presence.
The ruling is clear: the measurement is invalid.
2
Understand the Scenario
We have two transactions: first A buys from B, then A sells the same goods to C. Before the second sale, A measures the goods in the presence of C (the future second buyer). The question is whether C can rely on A's measurement.
C is present but not yet the buyer.
3
Follow the Hadith Reasoning
The hadith 'Do not sell food until you have taken possession of it' requires that measurement (صاع) be done by the seller and buyer. Since the second contract does not exist yet, A is not the seller and C is not the buyer, so the measurement is not attributable to the parties of that sale.
The hadith is cited as the primary evidence.
4
Consider After the Contract
If the measurement occurs after the second contract but in the absence of the second buyer, it is also invalid because delivery (تسلیم) must be done in the buyer's presence. Without the buyer, the measurement cannot constitute valid delivery.
This covers the post-contract scenario.
5
Derive the Condition
The underlying condition is that measurement must be performed by the actual buyer or seller of the contract, and delivery must occur in the buyer's presence. This prevents reliance on any prior measurement by a non-party.
This is a safeguard against uncertainty (gharar).

بيع الطعام ... الخ میں بائع اور مشتری کا صاع یعنی کیل یا وزن کرنا شرط ہے اور یہ نہ مانع کا صاع ہے اور نہ مشتری کا ۔ کیونکہ بائع اور مشتری کا تحقق عقد بیع کے بعد ہوتا ہے حالانکہ ابھی تک عقد بیع ہی موجود نہیں ہے اور جب عقد بیع موجود نہیں ہے تو بائع اور مشتری بھی موجود نہ ہوئے اور جب بائع اور مشتری موجود نہیں ہوئے تو یہ صاع نہ بائع کا ہوگا کیونکہ معتبر بائع یا مشتری کا صاع ہوتا ہے نہ کہ کسی دوسرے کا ۔ اور اگر بائع یعنی مشتری اول نے عقد ثانی کے بعد مشتری ثانی کی عدم موجودگی میں کیل کیا تو یہ بھی معتبر نہیں ہے کیونکہ کیل کر کے بیچ سپر د کی جاتی ہے اور کیل کے ذریعہ بیچ اس لیے سپرد کی جاتی ہے کہ کیل اور ناپنے سے میچ معلوم ہو جاتی ہے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ سپردگی مشتری کی موجودگی میں ہوتی ہے نہ کہ عدم موجودگی میں اس لیے مشتری ثانی کی عدم موجودگی میں تیل کرنا معتبر نہ ہوگا۔
The author of Hidayah says: The measurement done by the seller (i.e., the first buyer) before the second sale is not acceptable, even if he measured in the presence of the second buyer—i.e., in the presence of the person who will become the second buyer. The reason is that in the hadith 'Do not sell food until you have taken possession of it' etc., the condition is the measurement (sa') of the seller and the buyer, and this is neither the measurement of the seller nor of the buyer, because the seller and buyer come into existence after the contract is concluded, while the contract does not yet exist. And when the contract does not exist, there is no seller and buyer, so this measurement is not the measurement of the seller, since the acceptable measurement is that of the seller or the buyer, not of someone else. And if the seller (first buyer) measured after the second contract in the absence of the second buyer, that too is not acceptable, because delivery after measurement is done, and delivery is performed in the presence of the buyer, not in his absence. Therefore, measurement in the absence of the second buyer is not acceptable.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage quotes the author of Al-Hidayah (مرغيناني) to clarify that the first buyer's (now seller) measurement is not valid for the second buyer, even if done in the presence of the future second buyer. The reason is grounded in the hadith that requires the actual buyer and seller to perform the measurement (صاع). Since before the contract, the parties are not yet buyer and seller, their measurement does not count. After the contract, if the second buyer is absent, the measurement is also invalid because delivery (تسليم) must occur in the buyer's presence. Thus, the second buyer must personally measure or weigh the goods. This ruling emphasizes that the condition of measurement is tied to the actual parties of the contract, preventing reliance on any prior measurement.

Key Terms
صاع (ṣāʿ): A measurement unit for volume; used metonymically for the act of measuring or weighing.
تسلیم (taslīm): Delivery of goods to the buyer, which must be done in the buyer's presence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the first buyer's measurement invalid for the second buyer even if done in his presence?
A) Because the second buyer was not the actual buyer at that time.
B) Because the first buyer is not a trustworthy measurer.
C) Because the hadith requires two separate measurements.
D) Because the second buyer must always be absent during measurement.

Key Takeaway
The measurement of goods must be performed by the actual buyer or seller after the contract is formed, and delivery must occur in the buyer's presence.

One Measurement Sufficing in Resale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on measurement after a second sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of measurements required when a first buyer sells to a second buyer after the contract, and explain the rationale for preferring one measurement over two.

Core Idea
One measurement suffices after a second sale in the buyer's presence; two measures are needed only when two separate contracts are combined.

This passage addresses a practical question in sales: when the first buyer sells the goods to a second buyer, does a single measurement after the contract suffice, or must two measurements be made? Some scholars interpreted a hadith requiring 'two measures' literally, but the preferred Hanafi view clarifies that one measurement is enough, provided the buyer is present. Let's examine the reasoning behind this ruling and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is the number of measurements required after a first buyer (now seller) sells to a second buyer in the buyer's presence. Some scholars require two measurements; the correct Hanafi view holds that one suffices.
2
Analyze the proof for the two-measurement view
The proof is the apparent meaning of the hadith 'until two measures are conducted therein,' which seems to demand two separate measurements.
Hadith is from a salam context but used by some scholars broadly.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The preferred view argues that one measurement achieves all purposes: determining quantity, enabling delivery, and negating excess. The hadith applies only when two separate contracts are combined, as in the salam example.
The condition for the hadith's application is the combination of two contracts.
4
Distinguish the salam example
In salam, a person buys grain and orders an agent to take possession: first for the buyer, then for himself. Two measurements are required because two independent contracts are involved.
This clarifies why a simple resale differs.
5
Draw the practical conclusion
In the simple case of first buyer selling to second buyer, one measurement post-contract in the buyer's presence is sufficient. The hadith does not mandate two separate measures here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر بائع یعنی مشتری اول نے بیع ثانی کے بعد مشتری ثانی کی موجودگی میں ایک بار کیل کیا تو بعض حضرات کے قول کے مطابق صرف اس پر اکتفاء نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ مشتری ثانی کے واسطے دوسری بار کیل کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ ظاہر حدیث حتى يجرى فيه صاعان سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دوساع معتبر ہیں۔ ایک صاع بائع یعنی مشتری اول کا اور دوسرا صاع مشتری ثانی کا لیکن صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ صورت میں ایک بار کیل کرنے پر اکتفاء کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ کیل کرنے سے بیع بھی معلوم ہوگئی اور مشترکی خانی چونکہ موجود ہے اس لئے اس کی طرف سپرد کرنا بھی متحقق ہو گیا اور بیع کے مقدار مشروط سے زائد ہونے کے احتمال کی بھی نفی ہو گئی اور رہا حدیث کا مصداق تو یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ دو عقد جمع ہو جائیں جیسا کہ باب السلم میں بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک کر گندم خریدا اور رب المال کو قبضہ کرنے کا حکم دیا تو یہ قبضہ تو معتبر نہ ہوگا اور اگر یہ حکم دیا کہ پہلے میرے لیے قبضہ کرلے پھر اپنے لیے قبضہ کر لے ۔ پس رب کرلے المال نے ایک بار مسلم الیہ کے لیے کیل کیا اور دوسری بار اپنے لیے کیل کی تو جائز ہو جائیگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں دو عقد بشرط الکیل جمع ہو گئے ہیں اس لیے دو مرتبہ کیل کرنا ضروری ہے۔
And if the seller (i.e., the first buyer) after the second contract measured once in the presence of the second buyer, then according to the saying of some scholars, it is not sufficient to rely on this; rather, it is necessary for the second buyer to measure a second time, because the apparent meaning of the hadith 'until two measures are conducted therein' indicates that two measures are required: one measure by the seller (the first buyer) and one measure by the second buyer. But the correct view is that in the mentioned scenario, it is permissible to rely on one measurement, because with one measurement, the sale is known, and since the second buyer is present, delivery to him is also realized, and the possibility of the sale exceeding the contracted amount is negated. As for the application of the hadith, it is when two contracts are combined, as has been explained in the chapter of Salam: if a person bought one kurr of wheat and ordered the rabb al-mal to take possession, that possession is not acceptable; but if he ordered, 'First take possession for me, then take possession for yourself,' and the rabb al-mal measured once for the muslim ilayh and a second time for himself, it becomes permissible, because in that case two contracts are combined with the condition of measurement, so two measurements are necessary.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage addresses a disagreement regarding the number of required measurements after the second contract. Some scholars interpret the hadith 'until two measures are conducted' literally, requiring separate measures by the seller (first buyer) and the second buyer. However, the preferred (صحیح) view in the Hanafi school is that one measurement after the contract, done by the seller in the presence of the buyer, suffices for both. The reason: the purpose of measurement—to determine the exact quantity and enable delivery—is achieved with one measure, eliminating the risk of excess. The hadith's requirement of two measures applies only when two separate contracts are combined, as in the salam example where a single person acts as agent for both parties. In that case, two measurements are needed because two independent contracts are involved. This clarification prevents unnecessary repetition while maintaining the principle.

Key Terms
رب المال (rabb al-māl): The principal/investor in a salam contract, acting on behalf of another.
مسلم الیہ (muslam ilayh): The seller in a salam contract who receives the advance and delivers goods later.
کیل (qayl): Measurement of volume, especially of grain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many measurements are required when the first buyer sells to the second buyer after the contract in the second buyer's presence?
A) Two: one by the seller and one by the buyer.
B) One: a single measurement by the seller suffices.
C) None: measurement is not required in subsequent sales.
D) Two only if the buyer is absent.

Key Takeaway
In a resale after the contract, one measurement done by the seller in the buyer's presence is sufficient; the hadith's 'two measures' applies only when two separate contracts are combined.

Measurement in Food Sales and the Ruling on Counted Items
Explains measurement condition and intra-Hanafi dispute on counted items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on measurement in food sales and distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on counted items.

Core Idea
One measurement suffices in resale when the second buyer is present; counted items are not ribawi per the Sahibayn.

This passage delves into a critical condition in the sale of food: precise measurement to avoid gharar and riba. It resolves a potential misunderstanding about the number of measurements required and then navigates an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether counted items (like walnuts) must be recounted when resold. The correct view relies on the Sahibayn's position that counted items are analogous to produce, not weighed goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Measurement
The passage states that measurement (kayl/wazn) is a condition (shart) in the sale of food. Determine who must perform the measurement: it must be the seller or buyer, not a third party.
2
Understand the Presence Requirement
If the first buyer (now seller) measures after the second sale but in the absence of the second buyer, the measurement is invalid because delivery must occur in the buyer's presence.
3
Resolve the One vs. Two Measurements Debate
Some argue from the hadith 'حتى يجرى فيه صاعان' that two measurements are needed. The correct Hanafi view is that one measurement suffices when the second buyer is present, as it achieves knowledge of quantity and delivery.
The hadith applies only when two contracts conditional on measurement combine, e.g., in salam.
4
Analyze the Dispute on Counted Items
For items sold by count (maddud) like walnuts, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no recounting is needed because they are not ribawi. Imam Abu Hanifa analogizes them to weighed goods (mawzun), requiring counting before disposition.
The practical difference: under the Sahibayn, the second buyer can consume or resell without counting; under Abu Hanifa, counting is obligatory.
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the dispute: if walnuts are found to be more or fewer than contracted, how does each view handle the excess or deficiency? This clarifies the need for recounting.

Source Text

زائد مشتری کو سپر نہیں کرے گا اور اگر کم پڑ گئے تو مشتری حصہ نقصان بائع سے واپس لے لے گا یعنی اسی کے بقدر بائع سے ثمن واپس لے لیگا۔ اس لیے معدودی چیز میں تصرف کرنے سے پہلے ان کو شمار کرنا ضروری ہے شمار کرنے سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ موزونی چیز میں وزن کرنے سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
In the sale of food, it is a condition that the seller and buyer use a sa' (measure or weight). And this sa' is neither the sa' of the previous seller nor the buyer. Because the seller and buyer come into existence after the contract is concluded, whereas the contract has not yet come into existence. And when the contract does not exist, the seller and buyer also do not exist. And when they do not exist, this sa' cannot be attributed to them because the valid sa' is that of the seller or buyer, not of a third party. And if the seller (i.e., the first buyer) measured after the second contract in the absence of the second buyer, that is not valid either, because measurement is done for delivery, and the purpose of measurement is to know the quantity. And it is agreed that delivery takes place in the presence of the buyer, not in his absence. Therefore, measurement in the absence of the second buyer is not valid. And if the seller (first buyer) measured once in the presence of the second buyer after the second sale, according to some scholars it is not sufficient; a second measurement is necessary for the second buyer, because the apparent meaning of the hadith 'حتى يجرى فيه صاعان' indicates that two sa's are valid: one sa' of the seller (first buyer) and one sa' of the second buyer. However, the correct view is that one measurement is sufficient, because with one measurement the sale is known, and since the buyer is present, delivery to him is achieved, and the possibility of excess over the contracted quantity is negated. As for the application of the hadith, it applies when two contracts are combined, as explained in the chapter of Salam: if a person buys one kurr of wheat and orders the owner of capital to take possession, that possession is not valid; but if he orders, 'First take possession for me, then for yourself,' and the owner of capital measures once for the Muslim ilayhi and once for himself, it becomes permissible. In that case, two contracts conditional on measurement are combined, so two measurements are necessary. And if something is bought that is sold by counting, like walnuts and eggs, for example, one says, 'I buy these one thousand walnuts for one hundred rupees,' then according to the narration of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this is like produce (mazru')—if the person sells these walnuts with the condition of counting, it is not necessary for the second buyer to count again; rather, the second buyer may dispose of them without counting. The proof is that like produce, these are not ribawi goods. Thus, selling one walnut for two walnuts is permissible. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is like weighed goods (mawzun), because just as a weighed good in excess of the contracted quantity is not permissible for the buyer, similarly a counted good in excess of the contracted quantity is not permissible. Therefore, if someone buys one thousand walnuts for one hundred rupees and then finds them to be more than one thousand, the seller will not deliver the excess to the buyer; and if they are fewer, the buyer will deduct the corresponding amount from the price. Hence, before disposing of a counted item, it is necessary to count it; disposition before counting is not permissible, just as disposition before weighing is not permissible for a weighed item.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding measurement (kayl/wazn) in the sale of food (bai' al-ta'am). The author explains that when a first buyer resells food, the measurement must be done by the seller (first buyer) or the second buyer, not by a neutral third party. If the first buyer measures in the absence of the second buyer, it is invalid because delivery must occur in the presence of the buyer. However, if the second buyer is present, one measurement suffices, even though some scholars argue for two measurements based on the hadith 'حتى يجرى فيه صاعان'. The correct Hanafi position is that one measurement is enough when the contracts are separate; the hadith applies only when two measurement-conditional contracts are combined, as in salam. Then it discusses counted items (m'addud) like walnuts: according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), such items are like produce (non-ribawi) and do not require recounting by the second buyer, whereas Imam Abu Hanifa analogizes them to weighed goods (mawzun) requiring counting before disposal. The dispute hinges on whether counted items fall under ribawi categories.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A standard measure of volume used for measuring food in sales; in this text, it refers to the act of measurement (kayl/wazn).
معدود (maddud): Items sold by count, such as walnuts, eggs, or other individual countable objects.
موزون (mawzun): Items sold by weight, such as grains or metals; subject to strict measurement before disposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of food, when the first buyer resells to a second buyer in the presence of the second buyer, how many measurements are required according to the correct Hanafi view?
A) Two measurements – one by the first buyer and one by the second buyer.
B) One measurement is sufficient.
C) No measurement is required if both parties agree.
D) Measurement is only required if the food is sold by weight.

Key Takeaway
One measurement suffices in resale when the second buyer is present; counted items are not ribawi per the Sahibayn, so no recounting is needed.

Disposal of the Price Before Taking Possession
States the ruling that the seller may dispose of the price before qabd, with evidence from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disposing of the price before qabd, explain the reasoning based on ownership and non-specific nature of the price, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A seller may dispose of the price before taking possession because ownership transfers immediately and the price is non-specific, so no risk of contract annulment.

In this passage, the author explains a key Hanafi principle: the seller's rights over the price are not dependent on physical possession. Understanding this ruling clarifies how ownership and risk are treated differently for the price versus the sold item, resolving common doubts about pre-possession transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening sentence: disposal of the price before qabd is permissible (ja'iz). Note that this applies to both specific and non-specific prices.
The ruling is mubah (permissible), not wajib.
2
Analyze the reasoning
Find the two key reasons: (1) ownership (milk) is established upon contract, and (2) there is no gharar (risk of annulment) because the price is not made specific by specification.
The price is ghayr mu'ayyan – if destroyed, the buyer can substitute it.
3
Distinguish from the sold item
Contrast: the sold item (mabi') becomes specific and its destruction before delivery annuls the contract. The price does not become specific, so no annulment risk.
This distinction is crucial for understanding Hanafi sale law.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Companions exchanging the price (taking dinars for dirhams) before actually receiving the original price, with the Prophet's approval.
This is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala, but sufficient for establishing the ruling.
5
Conclude the permissibility
Synthesize: since the permitting factor (ownership) is present and the impediment (risk of annulment) is absent, disposal of the price is permissible.
This ruling is from zahir al-riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والتصرف في الثمن قبل القبض جائز لقيام المطلق وهو الملك وليس فيه عرر الانفساح بالهلاك لعدم تعينها بالتعين بخلاف المبيع
قبضہ سے پہلے من میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے کیونکہ تصرف کی اجازت دینے والی چیز یعنی ملک قائم ہے اور اس میں شمن ملاک کہ ہونے کی وجہ سے بیچ کے مسخ ہونے کا دھو کہ بھی نہیں ہے کیونکہ ثمن متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتا بر خلاف بیع کے۔۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عقد بیع کے بعد ثمن پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے بائع کے لیے شمن کے اندر تصرف کرنے کی اجازت ہے ثمن خواہ مالا تعین کے قبیلہ سے ہو جیسے نقود، خواہ ما یتعین کے قبیلہ سے ہو جیسے مکیلی یا موزونی چیز مثلاً اگر کسی نے ایک اونٹ ایک سو درہمہ کے عوض یا ایک گر گندم کے عوض فروخت کیا تو بائع کے لئے دراہم اور گندم کے بدلے دوسری چیز کا لینا جائز ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ شمن کے اندر تصرف کو جائز کر نیوالی چیز ملک ہے یعنی مالک اپنی مملوک چیز میں تصرف کر نی کا مجاز ہوتا ہے اور عقد زریچ کے بعد بائع شمن کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے خواہ اس پر قبضہ کیا ہو یا قبضہ نہ کیا ہو۔ اور تصرف سے مانع عقد بیع کے فسخ ہونے کا دھو کہ تھا لیکن یہاں شمن ہلاک ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد بیع کے نسخ ہونے کا دھوکہ بھی موجود نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ثمن متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتا۔ برخلاف مبیع کے کہ وہ متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے پس اگر شمن ہلاک ہو گیا تو مشتری اس کی جگہ دوسراشن ادا کر سکتا ہے اور جب دوسرا من ادا کر دیا گیا تو نبیع کے فسخ ہونے کا امکان باقی نہ رہا۔ حاصل یہ کہ جب تصرف کو جائز کرنے والی چیز یعنی ملک موجود ہے اور مانع تصرف منتفی ہے تو شمن کے اندر تصرف کے جائز ہونے میں کیا شبہ ہے۔ اس کی تائید حدیث ابن عمر سے بھی ہوتی ہے۔
قال ابن عمر رضی الله عنهما كنا نبيع الابل في البقيع فنا خذ مكان الدراهم الدنانير و مكان الدنانير الدراهم و كان يجوزه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ۔ ابن عمر رضی اللہ تعالی عنہما فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم لوگ بقیع میں اونٹ فروخت کرتے تھے پس دراہم کی جگہ دینا نیر اور دنا نیر کی جگہ دراہم لیتے تھے اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم بھی اس کو جائز قرار دیتے تھے ۔ ابن عمر کا منشاء یہ ہے کہ اگر شمن دراہم ہوتے تو ان کے بدلے دنا نیر لے لیا کرتے اور اگر شمن دینا نیر ہوتے تو ان کے بدلے دراہم لے لیا کرتے اور یہ مشن پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس میں تصرف کرنا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ بائع کے لیے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے شمن میں تصرف کرنے کی اجازت ہے۔
He said: Disposal of the price before taking possession is permissible because the basis (ownership) is established, and there is no risk of the contract being annulled due to destruction, because the price is not specified by specification, unlike the sold item.
[Urdu commentary: Disposal of the price before qabd is permissible because the thing that permits disposal, i.e., ownership, is established, and there is no risk of the contract being voided due to destruction, because the price is not made specific by specification, unlike the sold item. Explanation: After the contract, before the seller takes possession of the price, it is permissible for him to dispose of the price, whether it is from the category of non-specific things like currency, or from the category of specific things like measured or weighed items. For example, if someone sold a camel for one hundred dirhams or for one kurr of wheat, the seller may take another thing in exchange for the dirhams and wheat. The proof is that the thing that makes disposal permissible is ownership, i.e., an owner is authorized to dispose of his property, and after the contract, the seller becomes owner of the price, whether he has taken possession or not. The impediment to disposal was the risk of the contract being annulled, but here there is no risk of annulment due to destruction because the price is not specified by specification, unlike the sold item. If the price is destroyed, the buyer can pay another price instead, and when another price is paid, the contract is not annulled. So when the permitting factor (ownership) is present and the impediment is absent, there is no doubt about permissibility. This is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar.]
Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) said: We used to sell camels in al-Baqi' and take dinars instead of dirhams and dirhams instead of dinars, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) permitted that. [The meaning is that if the price was dirhams, they would take dinars instead, and vice versa; this is disposal of the price before taking possession. So it is established that the seller is permitted to dispose of the price before qabd.]
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This is a commentary on the ruling that a seller may dispose of the price (thaman) even before taking physical possession (qabd). The key reasoning is twofold: first, the seller becomes owner of the price immediately upon contract, so he has the right to use his property; second, the price is not 'ain (specific) – meaning its destruction does not annul the contract because the buyer can substitute it with another equivalent. This differs from the sold item (mabi'), which if destroyed before delivery, the contract is annulled. The hadith of Ibn Umar provides practical evidence: in the time of the Prophet, they would exchange the price (taking dinars for dirhams) before actually receiving the coins. This indicates that such disposition is permitted.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price paid or promised in a sale; may be currency or other goods specified in the contract.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the sold item or price.
ملك (milk): Ownership; the legal right to possess and dispose of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it permissible for the seller to dispose of the price before taking possession (qabd)?
A) Because the price is always in the form of currency.
B) Because ownership transfers upon contract, and the price is not specific.
C) Because the buyer agrees to it.
D) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade it.

Key Takeaway
A seller may dispose of the price before physical possession because ownership is established and the risk of contract annulment is absent due to the price's non-specific nature.

Post-Contract Modifications: Attachment or New Contract?
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on post-contract modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ziyada and hott after the contract and evaluate the opposing arguments from Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Post-contract increases or reductions attach to the original contract because parties can change its description.

This lesson examines a key dispute: whether a buyer's voluntary price increase or seller's reduction attaches to the original sale or creates a new contract. Abu Hanifa and the majority Hanafi view hold that such modifications attach (iltihaq), while Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue they form a new transaction. Understanding this dispute clarifies the flexibility of Hanafi contract law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the modifications
List the three post-contract changes considered: buyer increases price, seller increases goods, seller reduces price.
All are voluntary changes after the sale is concluded.
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa, these changes attach to the original contract (iltihaq). They are valid as part of the same transaction.
The key term is 'iltihaq' (attachment).
3
Analyze the opposing argument
Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that an increase would mean ownership in exchange for ownership, and a reduction would remove part of the price that already corresponds to the entire mabi'. Thus, they become new contracts.
Their reasoning is based on impossibility of altering a fully exchanged consideration.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the change is merely in description (e.g., from being at a profit to at a loss), and since parties have the right to annul, they have the right to change.
This is the core of the argument: authority to annul implies authority to modify.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, the original contract remains intact with modifications; no new contract is needed. Under the opposing view, the original contract is unaffected and a new separate transaction is formed.
Practical difference: e.g., if there is a defect in the original goods, under Hanafi the modification does not affect warranty periods.

Source Text

مشتری کا شمن میں اضافہ، بائع کا مبیع میں اضافہ اور بائع کے لیے شمن میں کمی کرنے کا حکم
قال ويجوز للمشترى ان يزيد للبائع فى الثمن ويجوز للبائع ان يزيد للمشترى في المبيع ويجوزان يحط عن الثمن ويتعلق الاستحقاق بجميع ذالك فالزيادة والحط يلتحقان باصل العقد عندنا وعند زفرو الشافعى لا يصحان على اعتبار الالتحاق بل على اعتبار ابتداء الصلة لهما انه لا يمكن تصحيح الزيادة ثمنا لانه يصير ملكه عوض ملكه فلا يلتحق باصل العقد وكذالك الحط لان كل الثمن صار مقابلا بكل المبيع فلا يمكن اخراجه فصار برا مبتدا ولنا انهما بالحط او الزيادة يغيران العقد من وصف مشروع الى وصف مشروع وهو كونه رابحا او خاسرا او عدلا ولهما ولاية الرفع فاولى ان يكون لهما ولاية التغير وصار كما
Ruling on the buyer increasing the price, the seller increasing the mabi', and the seller decreasing the price.
He said: It is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the mabi' for the buyer, and they may also reduce the price. The right to claim is related to all of that. So the increase and reduction attach to the original contract according to us (Hanafis). According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, they are not valid as attaching but rather as a new beginning. For them, it is not possible to validate the increase as a price because it would become ownership in exchange for ownership, so it does not attach to the original contract. Similarly, reduction because all the price is in exchange for all the mabi', so it cannot be extracted; thus it becomes a new matter. Our proof is that by a reduction or increase, they change the contract from one lawful description to another lawful description, such as being profitable, losing, or fair. And they have the authority to annul, so it is more appropriate that they have the authority to change. And it becomes like...
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage addresses intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences regarding post-contract changes to the price or goods. According to Abu Hanifa (and the Hanafi school), if the buyer voluntarily increases the price, or the seller increases the mabi', or the seller reduces the price, these modifications attach to and become part of the original contract (iltihaq). This is because they are changing the contract from one permissible description to another, and since the parties have the right to annul the contract (in certain circumstances), they can also make such amendments. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar who sometimes differed) and al-Shafi'i hold that such changes cannot attach to the original contract because an increase would mean one owns the same thing in return for one's own property (i.e., paradox), and a reduction would imply removing part of the price that has already been exchanged for the entire mabi'. Therefore, they consider these changes as new, separate transactions.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An increase in the price (by the buyer) or in the mabi' (by the seller) after the contract.
حط (hott): A reduction in the price by the seller after the contract.
التحاق (iltihaq): The legal attachment of a subsequent modification to the original contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal status of a buyer's voluntary increase in the price after the contract?
A) It is invalid because the price is fixed.
B) It attaches to the original contract and is valid.
C) It requires a new contract.
D) It is permissible only if the seller agrees.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, post-contract increases or reductions legally attach to the original sale because the parties have the authority to change the contract's description.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Post-Contract Modifications: Increase and Decrease in Price or Sold Item
Inter-madhhab dispute on post-contract price/item modifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on post-contract increases or decreases in price or sold item, state the opposing Shafi'i/Zufar view, evaluate the Hanafi proof, and identify the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) in murabahah and shuf'ah.

Core Idea
Post-contract changes to price or item attach to the original contract in Hanafi fiqh, unlike the opposing view that treats them as new gifts.

When parties modify the price or goods after a sale is concluded, is the change part of the original contract or a separate transaction? The Hanafi school argues that such modifications are valid and attach to the original contract, a position that affects profit calculations and pre-emption rights. This lesson explores the reasoning behind the Hanafi view and the counterargument from Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that post-contract increases and decreases are permissible and become attached to the original contract (multahaq bil asl). This includes buyer increasing price, seller increasing sold item, or seller decreasing price.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar argue these are new gifts (ibtida' sila) because an increase would mean the buyer pays for his own ownership, and a decrease leaves part of the price without consideration.
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response: The parties have authority to annul the contract, so they a fortiori have authority to modify its description. This is analogous to post-contract stipulations or cancellations of options (khiyar), which also attach to the original.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In murabahah, Hanafi treats the modification as part of the original, affecting profit calculation on the total new price; in shuf'ah, the pre-emptor can take at the reduced price but cannot be forced to take at the increased price.
5
Note the exception: increase after destruction
According to the apparent narration, an increase is invalid if the sold item is destroyed, while a reduction remains valid because the seller can still release part of the price.

ا تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری بائع کے لیے ثمن میں کچھ اضافہ کر دے تو جائز ہے مثلاً ایک غلام ایک سورد پسیہ میں خریدا پھر مشتری نے دس روپیہ کا اضافہ کر دیا تو یہ اضافہ کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح اگر بائع مبیع میں اضافہ کر دے یا شمن میں سے کچھ کم کر دے تو بھی جائز ہے مثلاً ایک شخص نے ایک سورد پہیہ کے عوض ایک من گندم فروخت کیا پھر اس میں دس کلو گندم کا اضافہ کر دیا یا ایک سورو پی یمن میں سے کم کر دیے تو جائز ہے۔ اور استحقاق اصل اور اضافہ شدہ دونوں کے ساتھ متعلق ہو گا چنانچہ شمن کے اندر اضافہ کی صورت میں بائع کو مبیع
Ruling on the buyer increasing the price, the seller increasing the sold item, and the seller decreasing the price. He said: It is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the sold item for the buyer, and it is permissible to reduce the price, and the entitlement (to the subject matter) is attached to all of that. So the increase and decrease are attached to the original contract according to us. According to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, they are not valid on the basis of attachment but rather on the basis of a new gift. Their proof is that it is not possible to validate the increase as price because it would become his ownership in exchange for his ownership, so it does not attach to the original contract. Similarly, the reduction because all of the price is in exchange for all of the sold item, so it is not possible to extract it, so it becomes a new gift. Our proof is that they, by reduction or increase, change the contract from one valid description to another valid description, which is being profitable, loss-making, or equal. And they have the authority to annul, so they have the authority to change a fortiori. This is like when they cancel an option or stipulate it after the contract; then when it becomes valid, it attaches to the original contract because the description of a thing is established by it, not by itself. Unlike the cancellation of the whole, which is not a change of description, so it does not attach. On the basis of attachment, the increase is not a substitute for his ownership. The effect of attachment appears in wala' and murabahah: it is permissible on the whole in increase, and he proceeds on the remainder in reduction. And in pre-emption, he takes what remains after reduction. The pre-emptor may take without the increase because the increase nullifies his established right, so they do not own it. Then increase is not valid after the destruction of the sold item according to the apparent narration because the sold item does not remain in a state in which taking compensation for it is valid, while the thing is established then attributed. Unlike reduction, because it is in a state where it is possible to extract the substitute for what corresponds to it, so it attaches to the original contract by attribution. Translation: And it is permissible for the buyer to increase the price for the seller, and it is permissible for the seller to increase the sold item for the buyer, and it is also permissible to reduce the price, and entitlement will attach to all of them. Increase and decrease, according to us, become attached to the original contract, while according to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, they are not valid on the basis of attachment but rather on the basis of a new gift. The proof of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zufar is that it is not possible to validate the increase as price because the buyer's ownership would become in exchange for his ownership, so it will not attach to the original contract. Similarly, reduction because the entire price is in exchange for the entire sold item, so it is not possible to extract it, so this becomes a new favor. Our proof is that by reduction or increase, they change the contract from one valid description to another valid description, which is the sale being profitable, loss-making, or equal. And they have the authority to rescind the sales contract, so they have the authority to change it a fortiori. This becomes like when they cancel an option or stipulate an option after the contract; then when this change is valid, it attaches to the original contract. On the basis of attachment, the increase is not in exchange for his ownership. The effect of attachment appears in sale by wala' and murabahah: in the case of increase, it is permissible on the whole; in the case of reduction, on the remainder. And in pre-emption, it appears such that in reduction, he takes what remains, and the pre-emptor may take without the increase because the increase would nullify his established right, so they do not own it. Then increase is not valid after the destruction of the sold item according to the apparent narration because the sold item does not remain in a state in which taking compensation for it is valid, whereas the thing is established then attributed. Unlike reduction, because it is in a state where it is possible to extract the substitute for what corresponds to it, so it attaches to the original contract by attribution. Explanation: The scenario is that if the buyer increases the price for the seller, it is permissible, e.g., buying a slave for one hundred rupees, then the buyer adds ten rupees. Similarly, if the seller increases the sold item or reduces the price, it is also permissible, e.g., a person sold one maund of wheat for one hundred rupees, then he adds ten kilos of wheat or reduces ten rupees. Entitlement will attach to both the original and the added portion.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding post-contract modifications to the price or sold item. The Hanafi school holds that such changes (increase or decrease) are valid and become attached to the original contract (multahaq bil asl). The opposing view, from Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, considers these as new independent acts (ibtida' sila) rather than modifications to the original. Their reasoning: an increase in price would mean the buyer is paying for his own ownership (since he already owns the item), and a decrease would leave part of the price without corresponding consideration. The Hanafi response: the parties have the authority to annul the contract entirely, so they a fortiori have the authority to modify its terms. This is compared to post-contract stipulations or cancellations of options, which also attach to the original. The practical effects of attachment appear in sales like wala' (consignment) and murabahah (cost-plus) and in pre-emption (shuf'ah): after an increase, the whole transaction is considered for profit calculations; after a reduction, only the remaining part. In pre-emption, the pre-emptor may take the property at the reduced price but cannot be forced to take at the increased price. Additionally, an increase is not valid after the sold item is destroyed (according to the apparent narration) because the item no longer exists to be exchanged, while a reduction remains valid because it only involves releasing a part of the price.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): An addition to the price or sold item after the contract is concluded.
حط (hatt): A reduction or decrease in the price after the contract.
التحاق (iltihāq): The legal attachment of a post-contract modification to the original contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a post-contract increase in price by the buyer?
A) It is invalid because the buyer cannot pay for what he already owns.
B) It becomes a separate gift from the buyer to the seller.
C) It attaches to the original contract, and the entire new price is considered for profit calculations.
D) It is valid only if the seller agrees to a new contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, post-contract increases and decreases in price or sold item are valid modifications that attach to the original contract, distinguishing them from new independent gifts.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Post-Sale Price Adjustments: Attachment vs New Gift/Discharge
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and practical consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that post-sale price increases and decreases attach to the original contract (ilhaq) and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i/Zufar view that they are separate gifts or discharges.

Core Idea
Post-sale price adjustments are part of the original sale, not new gifts or discharges.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses a classic dispute in Islamic commercial law: what happens when a buyer or seller voluntarily changes the price after the contract is already complete? The Hanafi school holds that such adjustments 'attach' to the original contract, treating it as if the contract was made on the modified terms. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, however, view them as new legal acts—a gift (hiba) for increases and a discharge (ibra) for decreases. Understanding this difference is crucial for properly calculating sales in tawliyah and murabahah, and for pre-emption (shuf'a). We will analyze the proofs of both sides and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: increases or decreases in price or object after the contract are valid and attach to the original contract as if the contract was originally made with the adjusted terms.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Know that Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar reject attachment. For them, an increase is a new gift (hiba) requiring possession, and a decrease is a discharge (ibra) that the buyer may reject.
They consider the original contract fixed once concluded.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand their reasoning: an increase would exchange the buyer's own property for his own property (invalid), and a decrease would leave part of the sold object without consideration or require a new contract.
They argue by impossibility of attaching a new term to a completed exchange.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi school rebuts: the adjustment only changes a description (wasf) of the contract (e.g., from profitable to loss-making), not the essence. Since parties can rescind the entire contract, they can a fortiori modify its description. This is analogous to dropping or stipulating options after the contract.
The Hanafi dalil uses qiyas on khiyar (options).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequences: In tawliyah and murabahah, Hanafis include the adjustment in the base cost; Shafi'is treat it separately. In shuf'a, the pre-emptor takes at the reduced price but cannot be forced to pay an increase. Also, increase after destruction of the sold object is invalid per Hanafi zahir al-riwaya, but decrease remains valid.
This shows how the difference affects real transactions.

Source Text
