Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Illa of Riba: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Explains riba hadith and disputes the effective cause of riba between Hanafis and Shafi'is

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i illa for riba al-fadl, identify the proof each school uses, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah) of the disagreement.

Core Idea
The Hanafi 'illa is genus+quantity; the Shafi'i 'illa is edibility/monetary value.

This passage delves into the core disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the effective cause ('illa) that triggers the prohibition of excess in exchange (riba al-fadl). Both schools agree that the prohibition is not limited to the six items named in the hadith, but they differ on what attribute justifies extending the ruling to other items. Understanding this dispute is crucial for applying the law of riba to new commodities and financial instruments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds as the 'illa for riba al-fadl. Note the two components: genus (jins) and quantity (qadr, i.e., measurability by weight or volume).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their proof
State the Shafi'i 'illa: edibility (tu'm) for foodstuffs and monetary value (thaman) for currencies. Understand their proof: the conditions of equality and hand-to-hand in the hadith indicate nobility, and only edibility/monetary value manifest nobility.
The passage provides their detailed proof from the hadith.
3
Analyze the basis of disagreement
Observe that both schools accept the same hadith but extract different 'illa due to differing views on what attribute is suitable (munasib) for the ruling. The Hanafi 'illa is broader (all measurable homogenous goods); the Shafi'i 'illa is narrower (food and money).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply both positions to a concrete example, such as copper for copper. Under the Hanafi 'illa, excess is riba; under the Shafi'i 'illa, it is not (since copper is not food or currency).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text is from a Hanafi source, so the Hanafi view is presented as the relied-upon position. However, the Shafi'i argument is presented fairly. Note that the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is indeed genus+quantity.

کا اس پر اجماع ہے کہ فضل اور زیادتی حرام ہونے کا حکم معلول ہے یعنی علت پر مبنی ہے کہ اگر علت پائی جائے گی تو ہوا یعنی حرمت فضل کا تحق ہوگا ورنہ اس کا حق نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اصحاب خواہر قیاس اور علت کا انکار کرتے ہیں اور حدیث میں مذکور چھ چیزوں کے ساتھ ربوا کو خاص کرتے ہیں مگر چونکہ ائمہ اربعہ کے نزدیک حکم ربوا معلول ہے اس لیے ربوا کی علت کا بیان ضروری ہے سو ملا حظہ ہو کہ ہمارے نزدیک ربوا کی علت قدر مع الجنس ہے چنانچہ حدیث میں مذکور چھ چیزوں کے علاوہ جہاں یہ علت پائی جائے گی وہیں ربوا تحقق ہوگا۔ مثلاً چونہ کا تبادلہ اگر چونہ کے ساتھ کیا گیا تو اس میں فضل اور زیادتی ربوا کہلائے گی کیونکہ دونوں عوض کیلی ہیں اور دونوں کی جنس بھی ایک ہے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر لو ہے، پیتل اور رانگ کو اس کے ہم جنس کے عوض فروخت کیا گیا تو کسی ایک جانب میں فضل اور زیادتی رہا شمار ہوگی کیونکہ دونوں عوض وزنی ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ متحد الجنس بھی ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ربوا کی علت مطعومات میں طعم ہے اور اثمان میں ثمن ہونا چنانچہ ہر اس چیز میں ربوا حرام ہوگا جس میں طعم ہونا یا من ہونا پایا جائے کے مطعوم سے مراد ہر وہ چیز جس کو عام طور پر کھایا جاتا ہو خواہ روزی بنا کر یا سالن بنا کر خواہ تلذذ اور تفکہ کے طور پر۔ اس تعریف کی بنیاد پر مطعومات میں میوے، اناج، سبزیاں اور تمام مسالے داخل ہو جائیں گے اور بقول علامہ بدرالدین عینی شمن سے مراد وہ ہے جو پیدائشی طور پر شمن ہو۔ جیسے سونا اور چاندی یا جس کے ثمن ہونے پر لوگوں نے اتفاق کر لیا ہو جیسے سکہ مروجہ۔ بہر حال امام شافعی کے نزدیک ربوا کی علت مطعومات میں طعم ہے اور اثمان میں شمن ہوتا ہے اور اس کی شرط جنس کا متحد ہونا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزد یک اموال ربوا میں اصل تو حرمت ہے لیکن ربوا کی حرمت سے چھٹکارہ دینے والی چیز دونوں عوضوں کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری ہے یعنی اگر علت ربوا پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں عوض برابر ہوں تو یہ عقد حرام نہ ہوگا، بلکہ مباح اور جائز ہو گا طعم اور ثمنیت کے علت ربوا ہونے پر حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اموال ربویہ کی خرید و فروخت کرنے میں دو شرطوں کی تصریح فرمائی ہے ایک عاقدین کا عوضین پر باہمی قبضہ کرنا جیسا کہ ید بید کے لفظ سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے دوسرے دونوں عوضوں کا مساوی اور برابر ہونا جیسا کہ لفظ مثلا بمثل سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے ان دونوں کا شرط ہونا اس طور پر ہے کہ بحالت نصب یہ دونوں لفظ ترکیب میں حال واقع ہیں۔ اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے یہ دونوں باتیں شرط ہوں گی اور رفع کی روایت کے مطابق یہ کہا جائے گا کہ یہ دونوں لفظ یعنی ید بید اور مثل بمثل لفظوں میں اگر چہ مرفوع ہیں لیکن معنی نصب ہی معتبر ہے اور نصب سے رفع کی طرف محض اس لئے عدول کیا گیا ہے تا کہ جملہ اسمیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے دوام اور ثبوت پر دلالت کرے پس جب نصب ہی معتبر ہے تو یہ دونوں باتیں یعنی نقابض اور مماثلت شرط ہو جائیں گے۔ بہر حال حدیث میں نقابض اور مماثلت کا شرط ہونا بصراحت وارد ہے اور ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے ہر ایک اس بات پر دال ہے کہ جس مال کے لیے یہ شرطیں لگائی گئیں ہیں وہ مال عزت و حرمت کے قابل ہے جیسے عقد نکاح کے لیے شہادت شاہدین کا شرط ہونا اور دوسرے معاملات میں شہادت شاہدین کا شرط نہ ہونا ملک بضع ( محل وطی ) کے قابل عزت و حرمت ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے پس مال کا عزیز اور محترم ہونا ثابت ہو گیا اور جب مال عزیز اور محترم ہے تو حرمت ربا کی علت ایسی چیز کو قرار دینا مناسب ہے جو مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرے اور جب ہم نے بنظر غائر دیکھا تو طعم اور ثمنیت دونوں چیزیں مال کی عزت اور حرمت کو ظاہر کرنے والی نظر آئیں طعم تو اس لیے مال کی عزت اور حرمت کو ظاہر کرتا ہے کہ طعم سے انسان کی زندگی باقی رہتی ہے کیونکہ اگر انسان کو مطعومات میسر نہ آئیں تو انسان بھوکا مر جائے گا اور نسل انسانی تباہ ہو جائے گی اور شمنیت اس لئے مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرتی ہے کہ ثمن انسان کے ان مقاصد اور مصالح کو پورا کرنے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ بنتا ہے جن پر انسان کی بقاء موقوف ہے پس جب طعم اور ثمنیت دونوں مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرتے ہیں تو حضرت امام شافعی نے مطعومات میں طعم کو اور اثمان میں شمنیت کو حرمت ربوا کی علت قرار دیا اور جنسیت اور قدر کو مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرنے میں چونکہ کوئی دخل نہیں ہے اس لیے ان کو علت ربوا قرار نہیں دیا گیا البتہ جنسیت کو خرمت ربوا کی شرط قرار دیا گیا اور حکم چونکہ شرط کے ساتھ وجود اور عدماً دائر ہوتا ہے اس لیے علت کے ساتھ اگر جنسیت بھی پائی جائے گی تو ر بوا حرام ہوگا اور اگر جنسیت نہ پائی گئی تو ر بوا حرام نہ ہوگا۔
Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, equal for equal, hand to hand. But if these categories differ, then sell as you wish as long as it is hand to hand. This hadith is transmitted in two ways according to grammar: one with the six words and the word like in the nominative case, in which case there is an implied genitive construction: the sale of dates for dates or the sale of gold for gold, like for like. 'Sale of dates' is the subject and 'like' is its predicate. In the other narration, these words and the word like are in the accusative case. In this case, the imperative verb 'sell' is implied: 'sell the dates' etc. These words are accusative as objects of 'sell', and the word 'like' is accusative as a circumstantial adverb. In the hadith, 'like for like' means that the two countervalues are equal in measure or weight, and 'hand to hand' means that possession of both countervalues takes place in the session of contract. The conclusion is that in case of unity of quantity and unity of type, equality in measure or weight is a condition, and possession of both countervalues is also a condition.
The ruling is caused (ma'lul) by consensus of the practitioners of qiyas. But the 'illa according to us is what we have mentioned, and according to al-Shafi'i, it is edibility (tu'm) in foodstuffs and monetary value (thaman) in currencies, with kinship (jinsiyya) as a condition and equality as a means of release. The basis for him is prohibition because the Lawgiver explicitly stated two conditions: hand-to-hand possession and equality. All of this indicates nobility and significance, just as requiring witnesses in marriage indicates nobility. Therefore, the ruling is attributed to a cause appropriate for manifesting nobility and significance, namely edibility because human life depends on it, and monetary value because wealth, which is the basis of interests, depends on it. Kinship has no effect in this, so we made it a condition, and the ruling may revolve around a condition.
Translation: The ruling mentioned in the hadith is, by consensus of the mujtahids, caused (ma'lul). But according to us, the 'illa is what we mentioned, and according to Imam al-Shafi'i, in foodstuffs it is edibility, and in currencies it is monetary value. Its condition is kinship, and equality is its release. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, prohibition is the basis because the Lawgiver explicitly stated two conditions: mutual possession and equality. Each condition indicates nobility and significance, just as the condition of witnessing in marriage indicates nobility. So the ruling should be attributed to a cause appropriate for manifesting nobility and significance, and that is edibility because human life depends on it, and monetary value because the preservation of wealth, which is the basis of interests, depends on it. Kinship has no role in this, so we made it a condition, and the ruling revolves around the condition. Commentary: The author of al-Hidayah says that all mujtahids agree that the ruling of prohibition of excess (riba) is caused, i.e., based on a cause. If the cause is present, then the prohibition materializes; otherwise not, even though the Zahiris deny qiyas and 'illa and restrict riba to the six items mentioned in the hadith. But since the four Imams consider the ruling of riba to be caused, it is necessary to explain the 'illa of riba. Consider that according to us, the 'illa of riba is quantity with genus. Thus, wherever this cause is found beyond the six items, riba will occur. For example, if lime is exchanged for lime, any excess will be riba because both countervalues are measured and of the same genus. Similarly, if copper, brass, or tin are sold for the same genus, any excess in one side will be riba because both are weighed and of the same genus. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the 'illa of riba is edibility in foodstuffs and monetary value in currencies. So riba will be prohibited in everything in which edibility or monetary value is found. By 'foodstuff' is meant everything that is commonly eaten, whether as bread or curry, or for pleasure and enjoyment. Based on this definition, foodstuffs include fruits, grains, vegetables, and all spices. According to Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni, 'monetary value' means that which is inherently a medium of exchange, like gold and silver, or that which people have agreed upon as a medium of exchange, like current coinage. In short, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the 'illa of riba is edibility in foodstuffs and monetary value in currencies, and its condition is unity of type. According to him, prohibition is the basis in ribawi goods, but the means of release from prohibition is equality between the two countervalues. That is, if the two countervalues are equal despite the presence of the 'illa, then the transaction is not prohibited but permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence for edibility and monetary value being the 'illa of riba is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) explicitly stated two conditions for buying and selling ribawi goods: one is mutual possession of the countervalues, as understood from the phrase 'hand to hand', and the other is equality of the two countervalues, as understood from the phrase 'like for like'. That these two are conditions is derived from the fact that in the accusative reading, these two phrases are circumstantial (hal), and a circumstantial clause indicates a condition. Therefore, these two matters are conditions. According to the nominative reading, the meaning of accusative is considered, and the shift from accusative to nominative is only to indicate permanence and continuity. So when the accusative meaning is considered, these two matters become conditions. In any case, the hadith explicitly states that mutual possession and equality are conditions. Each of these two conditions indicates that the wealth for which these conditions are set is worthy of nobility and significance, just as the condition of witnesses for marriage indicates that the right of sexual enjoyment is worthy of nobility. Thus, the wealth is established as noble and significant. When the wealth is noble and significant, it is appropriate to make the 'illa of prohibition of riba something that manifests its nobility and significance. Upon careful consideration, edibility and monetary value are both seen to manifest the nobility and significance of wealth. Edibility manifests nobility because human life depends on it; if foodstuffs were not available, humans would starve and the human race would perish. Monetary value manifests nobility and significance because it is the means to achieve the interests on which human survival depends. Since both edibility and monetary value manifest nobility and significance, Imam al-Shafi'i made edibility the 'illa for prohibition of riba in foodstuffs and monetary value in currencies, and he did not make kinship and quantity the 'illa because they have no role in manifesting nobility. However, he made kinship a condition for prohibition of riba, and since the ruling revolves with the condition in existence and non-existence, if kinship is present along with the cause, then riba is prohibited; if kinship is not present, then riba is not prohibited.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the effective cause ('illa) of riba. The author first explains the grammar of the famous riba hadith (the six items: gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) to establish that the conditions of equality (مثلاً بمثل) and hand-to-hand possession (يداً بيد) are textual requirements. Then he presents the core dispute: while all mujtahids agree that the prohibition of excess in exchange is caused (i.e., subject to qiyas), the Hanafis and Shafi'is differ on what the 'illa is.

The Hanafi position (mentioned as 'عندنا' in the Arabic text): The 'illa is genus (جنس) combined with quantity (قدر). That is, whenever two items are of the same genus and are measurable (by weight or volume), any excess in exchange is riba, regardless of whether the items are food or not. The author provides examples: lime for lime, copper for copper — these are not food but are measured/weighed and of the same genus, so excess is riba.

The Shafi'i position: The 'illa is edibility (طعم) in foodstuffs and monetary value (ثمن) in currencies. For food, whatever is commonly eaten, including fruits, grains, vegetables, spices; for currencies, gold, silver, or any agreed-upon medium of exchange (like modern coins). Kinship (جنس) is a condition, not the 'illa itself. Equality (مساواة) is a means of release from prohibition: if the amounts are equal, the transaction is allowed despite the presence of the 'illa.

The passage then explains the Shafi'i proof: The hadith explicitly mentions two conditions (hand-to-hand and equality). These conditions indicate that the items involved are noble and significant, similar to the condition of witnesses in marriage. Edibility and monetary value are appropriate causes because they directly relate to human survival and interests, thus manifesting nobility. Quantity and genus do not manifest nobility, so they are not the 'illa.

The Hanafi response is implicit in the earlier statement: the 'illa is quantity with genus. The passage does not provide a rebuttal here but states the Hanafi view and gives examples. The reliance is on the fact that the hadith mentions six specific items, but the Hanafis extend the ruling by qiyas to any item that shares the 'illa of genus and quantity.

The commentary concludes that the ruling (prohibition) revolves around the condition: if the condition of kinship is present along with the cause, riba is prohibited; otherwise not. This is the Shafi'i view; for Hanafis, kinship is part of the cause itself.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The effective cause that justifies extending a ruling via qiyas. Both schools agree that the prohibition of riba is based on a cause that can be applied beyond the textual cases.
طعم (tu'm): Edibility as a generic characteristic of foodstuffs that are commonly consumed. Not limited to nutritional value; includes fruits, vegetables, spices.
ثمنية (thimaniyya (or thaman)): Monetary value: the quality of being used as a medium of exchange, either inherently (gold, silver) or by convention (coins).
قدر مع الجنس (qadr ma'a al-jins): Quantity with genus: the combination of being measurable (by weight or volume) and sharing the same species/genus.
يداً بيد (yadan bi-yad): Hand-to-hand: immediate possession and delivery of both countervalues in the same contract session. This is a condition for the validity of the exchange to avoid riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effective cause ('illa) for the prohibition of riba al-fadl (excess) in exchange?
A) Edibility (tu'm) in foodstuffs and monetary value (thaman) in currencies
B) Quantity (qadr) combined with genus (jins)
C) Hand-to-hand possession (yadan bi-yad) alone
D) The specific items mentioned in the hadith only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'illa for riba al-fadl is genus plus quantity, making any excess in a homogeneous measurable good prohibited, while the Shafi'i 'illa restricts prohibition to foodstuffs (by edibility) and currencies (by monetary value).

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi and Shafi'i Dispute on the Illa of Riba
Explains the Shafi'i and Hanafi positions on the effective cause of riba with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the effective cause of riba and evaluate the arguments each school uses to support its position.

Core Idea
The effective cause of riba is quantity with genus in Hanafi fiqh, but edibility or price in Shafi'i fiqh.

The prohibition of riba in sales is agreed upon, but the schools differ on which attribute of an item triggers the ruling. This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on the effective cause ('illa) of riba. You will learn the evidence each school presents and understand the practical consequences of this disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the effective cause of riba is quantity with genus (kayl or wazn with jins). Any excess in exchange of same-genus measured/weighed items is riba. Quality is not considered.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: the effective cause is edibility (tu'm) for food items and price (thamaniyyah) for monetary items. The condition is unity of genus.
Shafi'is define edibility broadly to include fruits, grains, vegetables, spices. Price includes gold, silver, and agreed-upon currency.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'is cite the hadith 'yadan bi-yadin mithlan bi-mithlin' (hand in hand, like for like), interpreting the accusative phrases as circumstantial (hal), making possession and equivalence conditions. They argue that edibility sustains life and price fulfills essential needs, thus they manifest the property's value, making them suitable as effective causes.
The Shafi'i argument emphasizes that the conditions indicate the property's sanctity, so the effective cause must manifest that sanctity.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis interpret 'mithlan bi-mithlin' as making equivalence a condition in sale itself, not just for riba avoidance. They argue that quality is not considered because it is not customarily counted as disparity, and considering edibility would close many permissible sales. They cite 'al-jayyidu wa al-radiyyu sawa'' (the good and bad are equal).
The Hanafi response focuses on the purpose of the hadith: to realize the meaning of sale (exchange) and protect property.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, for food items sold by count (e.g., eggs, fruits not measured by weight), Hanafis do not consider riba applicable because they are not measured/weighed, while Shafi'is consider riba if there is surplus because edibility is present. For monetary items, Hanafis consider gold/silver ribawi only by weight; Shafi'is consider them ribawi because they are prices.
The practical difference affects which sales are permissible without restriction.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد
کیا گیا تو کسی ایک جانب میں فضل اور زیادتی رہا شمار ہوگی کیونکہ دونوں عوض وزنی ہونے کے ساتھ ساتھ متحد الجنس بھی ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ربوا کی علت مطعومات میں طعم ہے اور اثمان میں ثمن ہونا چنانچہ ہر اس چیز میں ربوا حرام ہوگا جس میں طعم ہونا یا من ہونا پایا جائے کے مطعوم سے مراد ہر وہ چیز جس کو عام طور پر کھایا جاتا ہو خواہ روزی بنا کر یا سالن بنا کر خواہ تلذذ اور تفکہ کے طور پر۔ اس تعریف کی بنیاد پر مطعومات میں میوے، اناج، سبزیاں اور تمام مسالے داخل ہو جائیں گے اور بقول علامہ بدرالدین عینی شمن سے مراد وہ ہے جو پیدائشی طور پر شمن ہو۔ جیسے سونا اور چاندی یا جس کے ثمن ہونے پر لوگوں نے اتفاق کر لیا ہو جیسے سکہ مروجہ۔ بہر حال امام شافعی کے نزدیک ربوا کی علت مطعومات میں طعم ہے اور اثمان میں شمن ہوتا ہے اور اس کی شرط جنس کا متحد ہونا ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزد یک اموال ربوا میں اصل تو حرمت ہے لیکن ربوا کی حرمت سے چھٹکارہ دینے والی چیز دونوں عوضوں کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری ہے یعنی اگر علت ربوا پائے جانے کی صورت میں دونوں عوض برابر ہوں تو یہ عقد حرام نہ ہوگا، بلکہ مباح اور جائز ہو گا طعم اور ثمنیت کے علت ربوا ہونے پر حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اموال ربویہ کی خرید و فروخت کرنے میں دو شرطوں کی تصریح فرمائی ہے ایک عاقدین کا عوضین پر باہمی قبضہ کرنا جیسا کہ ید بید کے لفظ سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے دوسرے دونوں عوضوں کا مساوی اور برابر ہونا جیسا کہ لفظ مثلا بمثل سے مفہوم ہوتا ہے ان دونوں کا شرط ہونا اس طور پر ہے کہ بحالت نصب یہ دونوں لفظ ترکیب میں حال واقع ہیں۔ اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے۔ اس لیے یہ دونوں باتیں شرط ہوں گی اور رفع کی روایت کے مطابق یہ کہا جائے گا کہ یہ دونوں لفظ یعنی ید بید اور مثل بمثل لفظوں میں اگر چہ مرفوع ہیں لیکن معنی نصب ہی معتبر ہے اور نصب سے رفع کی طرف محض اس لئے عدول کیا گیا ہے تا کہ جملہ اسمیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے دوام اور ثبوت پر دلالت کرے پس جب نصب ہی معتبر ہے تو یہ دونوں باتیں یعنی نقابض اور مماثلت شرط ہو جائیں گے۔ بہر حال حدیث میں نقابض اور مماثلت کا شرط ہونا بصراحت وارد ہے اور ان دونوں شرطوں میں سے ہر ایک اس بات پر دال ہے کہ جس مال کے لیے یہ شرطیں لگائی گئی ہیں وہ مال عزت و حرمت کے قابل ہے جیسے عقد نکاح کے لیے شہادت شاہدین کا شرط ہونا اور دوسرے معاملات میں شہادت شاہدین کا شرط نہ ہونا ملک بضع ( محل وطی ) کے قابل عزت و حرمت ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے پس مال کا عزیز اور محترم ہونا ثابت ہو گیا اور جب مال عزیز اور محترم ہے تو حرمت ربا کی علت ایسی چیز کو قرار دینا مناسب ہے جو مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرے اور جب ہم نے بنظر غائر دیکھا تو طعم اور ثمنیت دونوں چیزیں مال کی عزت اور حرمت کو ظاہر کرنے والی نظر آئیں طعم تو اس لیے مال کی عزت اور حرمت کو ظاہر کرتا ہے کہ طعم سے انسان کی زندگی باقی رہتی ہے کیونکہ اگر انسان کو مطعومات میسر نہ آئیں تو انسان بھوکا مر جائے گا اور نسل انسانی تباہ ہو جائے گی اور شمنیت اس لئے مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرتی ہے کہ ثمن انسان کے ان مقاصد اور مصالح کو پورا کرنے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ بنتا ہے جن پر انسان کی بقاء موقوف ہے پس جب طعم اور ثمنیت دونوں مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرتے ہیں تو حضرت امام شافعی نے مطعومات میں طعم کو اور اثمان میں شمنیت کو حرمت ربوا کی علت قرار دیا اور جنسیت اور قدر کو مال کی عزت و حرمت کو ظاہر کرنے میں چونکہ کوئی دخل نہیں ہے اس لیے ان کو علت ربوا قرار نہیں دیا گیا البتہ جنسیت کو خرمت ربوا کی شرط قرار دیا گیا اور حکم چونکہ شرط کے ساتھ وجود اور عدماً دائر ہوتا ہے اس لیے علت کے ساتھ اگر جنسیت بھی پائی جائے گی تو ر بوا حرام ہوگا اور اگر جنسیت نہ پائی گئی تو ر بوا حرام نہ ہوگا۔

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد هشتم
۲۹۳
احناف کی دلیل
كتاب البيوع
التقابل
ولنا انه أوجب المماثلة شرطا فى البيع وهو المقصود بسوقه تحقيقا لمعنى البيع اذ هو ينبئى عن و ذالك بالتماثل اوصيانة لاموال الناس عن التوى اوتتميما للفائدة باتصال التسليم به ثم يلزم عند قوته حرمة الربواو المماثلة بين الشيأين باعتبار الصورة والمعنى والمعيار يسوى الذات والجنسية تسوي المعنى فيظهر الفضل على ذالك فيتحقق الربوا لان الربوا هو الفضل المستحق لاحد المتعاقدين في المعاوضة الخالي عن عوض شرط فيه ولا يعتبر الوصف لانه لا يعد تفاوتا عرفا اولان في اعتباره سد باب البياعات اولقوله عليه السلام جيدها ورديها سواء والطعم والثمنية من اعظم وجوه المنافع والسبيل في مثلها الطلاق بابلغ الوجوه لشدة الاحتياج اليها دون التضييق فيه فلا معتبر بما ذكره ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیج میں مماثلت کو شرط بنا کر ثابت کیا ہے اور بیان حدیث کا یہی مقصد ہے معنی بیع کو ثابت کرنے کے لیے اس لیے کہ لفظ بیچ مقابلہ کی خبر دیتا ہے اور مقابلہ مماثلت سے ہوگا یا لوگوں کے اموال کو ہلاک ہونے سے بچانے کے لیے یا بیچ کے ساتھ سپردگی مل کر بیع کا فائدہ پورا کرنے کے لیے پھر مماثلت فوت ہونے کے وقت حرمت ربوا لا زم آئے گی اور دو چیزوں کے درمیان مماثلت صورت اور معنی کے اعتبار سے ہوتی ہے اور معیار ( پیمانہ ) ذات میں برابری کرتا ہے اور ہم جنس ہونا معنی میں برابری کرتا ہے اس زیادتی اسی پر ظاہر ہوگی اور ربا تحقق ہوگا کیونکہ ربوا یہی ہے کہ معاوضہ میں عاقدین میں سے ایک کیلئے ایسی زیادتی ہو جو عوض سے خالی ہے اور عقد میں مشروط ہے اور وصف کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ عرف میں اس کو تفاوت شمار نہیں کرتے یا اس لیے کہ اسکا اعتبار کرنے میں خرید و فروخت کے دروازے بند ہو جائیں گے۔ یا اس لیے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ اموال ربویہ کا کھرا اور کھوٹا ہونا برابر ہے اور منافع مالی کی وجود میں سے ظلم اور حمیت بڑی وجہ ہے اور اس میں راہ ابلغ وجوہ کے ساتھ توسع دینا ہے کیونکہ اس کی طرف حاجت شدید ہے نہ کہ اس میں تنگی کی جائے پس جو کچھ امام شافعی نے ذکر فرمایا ہے اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہو سکتا۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں احناف کی طرف سے قدر مع الجنس کے علت ربوا ہونے پر دلیل بیان کی گئی ہے۔ دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حدیث مثلاً بمثل کے ذریعہ شارع نے بیج کے اندر مماثلت اور برابری کو شرط قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ مثلاً بمثل ترکیب نحوی کے اعتبار سے حال ہے اور حال شرط ہوتا ہے اس لیے اموال ربویہ کی بیچ میں مماثلت کا ہونا ضروری اور شرط ہے اور بیان حدیث سے مقصود بھی یہی ہے که اموال ربویہ کی بیع میں مماثلت پائی جائے کیونکہ حدیث کے معنی ہیں بیچ ہذہ الاشیاء مثال بمثل اور بمثل کا باء الصاق کے لیے ہے اور یوا صیغہ امر وجوب کے لیے ہے حالانکہ بیج واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ مباح ہے اس لیے صیغہ امر کا تعلق اس حال کے ساتھ ہو گا جو شرط ہے اب ترجمہ یہ ہو گا کہ ان چیزوں کو وصف مماثلت کے ساتھ فروخت کر د یعنی فروخت کرنا تو مباح ہے لیکن اگر فروخت کرو تو شرط مماثلت کی رعایت ضروری ہے۔ علامہ بدرالدین اور صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ حدیث بیان کرنے سے مقصود، مماثلت کا واجب ہونا تین وجھوں سے ہے پہلی وجہ تو یہ کہ عوضین کے درمیان مماثلت اور برابری پائے جانے کی وجہ سے بیچ کے معنی متحقق ہو جائیں گے اور اگر جماثلت اور برابری نہ ہو تو بیع کے معنی متحقق نہ ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ بیع نام ہے مبادلۃ المال بمال کا اور مبادلۃ باب مفاعلہ سے ہے اور مفاعلة کا خاصہ چونکہ اشتراک ہے اس لیے وہ اس کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ متحد انس میں عوضین میں سے احد العوضین کا ہر ہر جز دوسرے عوض کے ہر ہر
Chapter of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 8. If [the exchange] takes place, then excess and increase in one side will be considered riba because both countervalues are both weight-based and of the same genus. And according to Imam Shafi'i, the effective cause of riba in food items is edibility (tu'm) and in monetary items is being a price (thamaniyyah). Consequently, riba will be prohibited in every item in which edibility or being a price is found. By edibility is meant every item that is commonly eaten, whether as a staple or as a curry, or for pleasure and delight. Based on this definition, edibles include fruits, grains, vegetables, and all spices. According to Allamah Badr al-Din al-Ayni, by price (thaman) is meant that which is inherently a price, like gold and silver, or that which people have agreed upon as a price, like current coinage. In any case, according to Imam Shafi'i, the effective cause of riba in food items is edibility and in monetary items is being a price, and its condition is unity of genus. And according to Imam Shafi'i, the original ruling in ribawi properties is prohibition, but the thing that removes prohibition is equality and equivalence between the two countervalues. That is, if the effective cause of riba is present and the two countervalues are equal, then the contract is not prohibited, but rather permissible and lawful. In support of edibility and price being the effective cause of riba, Imam Shafi'i's evidence is that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ explicitly stipulated two conditions in the sale of ribawi properties: one is that the contracting parties mutually take possession of the countervalues, as understood from the phrase 'yadan bi-yadin' (hand in hand), and the second is that the two countervalues be equal and equivalent, as understood from the phrase 'mithlan bi-mithlin' (like for like). These two are conditions in the sense that in the case of nasb (accusative case), these two phrases are in the status of hal (circumstantial clause), and hal indicates a condition. Therefore, these two matters are conditions. According to the tradition of raf' (nominative), it would be said that these two phrases, i.e., 'yadan bi-yadin' and 'mithlan bi-mithlin', even if they are in the nominative, the meaning of accusative is considered, and the shift from accusative to nominative is only to indicate permanence and continuity through being a nominal sentence. So when the accusative is considered, these two matters, i.e., taking possession and equivalence, become conditions. In any case, the hadith explicitly states that taking possession and equivalence are conditions. And each of these two conditions indicates that the property for which these conditions are stipulated is worthy of respect and sanctity. Just as the condition of having two witnesses for marriage, and the absence of that condition in other transactions, indicates that the right of sexual intercourse (mahall al-wat') is worthy of respect and sanctity. Thus, the property is established as valuable and sacred. And when property is valuable and sacred, it is appropriate to make the effective cause of the prohibition of riba something that manifests its value and sanctity. When we look deeply, we see that edibility and price are both things that manifest the value and sanctity of property. Edibility manifests value and sanctity because life is sustained through edibles; if a person does not get edibles, he will die of hunger and the human race will perish. And price manifests value and sanctity because price serves as a means to fulfill the purposes and interests on which human survival depends. So when both edibility and price manifest the value and sanctity of property, Imam Shafi'i made edibility the effective cause of riba in food items and price in monetary items. And since genus and quantity have no role in manifesting value and sanctity, they were not made the effective cause of riba. However, genus was made a condition for the prohibition of riba, and since the ruling revolves with the condition in existence and non-existence, if genus is also present with the effective cause, then riba will be prohibited, and if genus is not present, then riba will not be prohibited. 

Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 8. Page 293. The Hanafi evidence. Chapter of Sales. Al-Taqabul. And we have [evidence] that he (ﷺ) made equivalence a condition in sale, and that is the purpose of its mention, to realize the meaning of sale, for it (sale) indicates exchange, and that is through equivalence, or to protect people's property from loss, or to complete the benefit by connecting delivery with it. Then when it (equivalence) is lost, the prohibition of riba becomes necessary. Equivalence between two things is in terms of form and meaning: the measure equalizes the substance, and genera equalize the meaning. Then excess appears on that, and riba is realized because riba is an excess that is due to one of the contracting parties in a commutative contract, devoid of any countervalue, and stipulated in the contract. And quality (wasf) is not considered because it is not regarded as disparity customarily, or because considering it would close the door of sales, or because the Prophet ﷺ said, "Its good and bad are equal." And edibility and price are among the greatest aspects of benefit, and the way in such matters is expansion through the most effective means due to severe need, not restriction. So what Imam Shafi'i mentioned is not to be considered. 

Translation: And our evidence is that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ established equivalence as a condition in sale, and this is the purpose of the hadith, to establish the meaning of sale, because the word 'sale' informs of exchange, and exchange is achieved through equivalence, or to protect people's property from destruction, or to complete the benefit by combining delivery with sale. Then when equivalence is lost, the prohibition of riba becomes necessary. And equivalence between two things is in terms of form and meaning. The measure (scale) equalizes in substance, and being of the same genus equalizes in meaning. Then the excess will appear on that, and riba will be realized because riba is that excess which is for one of the contracting parties in a commutative contract, devoid of a countervalue, and it is stipulated in the contract. And quality (attribute) will not be considered because customarily it is not counted as disparity, or because considering it would close the doors of buying and selling, or because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said that the good and bad of ribawi properties are equal. And the financial benefits [include] oppression and stringency are a great reason, and in this matter expansion through the most effective ways is to be adopted because there is severe need, not restriction. So whatever Imam Shafi'i mentioned cannot be considered.

Explanation: In this passage, the evidence from the Hanafis is given for quantity with genus (qadr ma'a al-jins) being the effective cause of riba. The gist of the evidence is that through the hadith 'mithlan bi-mithlin', the Lawgiver has made equivalence and equality a condition in sale, because the construction 'mithlan bi-mithlin' is a circumstantial clause (hal) grammatically, and hal indicates a condition. Therefore, in the sale of ribawi properties, equivalence is necessary and a condition. And the purpose of the hadith is also that equivalence be present in the sale of ribawi properties because the meaning of the hadith is 'Sell these things like for like', and the 'ba' in 'bi-mithlin' is for attachment, and 'bi'a' is a command form for obligation, even though sale is not obligatory but permissible. Therefore, the command form relates to the circumstantial clause which is a condition. Now the translation would be: 'Sell these things with the attribute of equivalence', i.e., selling is permissible, but if you sell, observing the condition of equivalence is necessary. Allamah Badr al-Din and Sahib al-Inayah have said that the purpose of the hadith is to make equivalence obligatory for three reasons: First, because with the presence of equivalence and equality between the countervalues, the meaning of sale is realized; and if there is no equivalence, the meaning of sale is not realized, because sale is called the exchange of property for property (mubadalah al-mal bi al-mal), and 'mubadalah' is on the pattern of mufa'alah, and the characteristic of mufa'alah is reciprocity, so it requires that in the same genus, every part of one countervalue corresponds to every part of the other.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the effective cause ('illa) of riba. The commentary begins by outlining the Shafi'i position: for riba to be prohibited in an exchange, the effective cause must be either edibility (tu'm) for food items or being a price (thamaniyyah) for monetary items. Edibility is defined as anything commonly eaten, including fruits, grains, vegetables, and spices. Price (thaman) is defined as that which is inherently a price (gold/silver) or that which people agree upon as currency. Imam Shafi'i supports this with the hadith 'yadan bi-yadin mithlan bi-mithlin' (hand in hand, like for like), interpreting the accusative phrases as circumstantial conditions (hal), making possession and equivalence conditions that indicate the property's value and sanctity. He argues that since edibility sustains life and price facilitates essential needs, both manifest the property's value, making them suitable as effective causes. Genus and quantity are merely conditions, not causes.

Then the text presents the Hanafi position and their evidence (dalil). The Hanafis argue that the hadith 'mithlan bi-mithlin' actually makes equivalence (tamathul) a condition in the sale itself, and the purpose is to realize the meaning of sale as exchange, protect property from loss, or complete the benefit. Equivalence is considered in both form (through measure/weight) and meaning (through genus). The effective cause of riba, according to Hanafis, is quantity with genus (qadr ma'a al-jins): if both countervalues are of the same genus and are measured or weighed, any excess is riba. Quality or other attributes are not considered because they are not customarily counted as disparity, and considering them would close the door of legitimate sales. The Hanafis cite another hadith, 'The good and bad of it are equal', indicating that differences in quality do not matter. They also argue that edibility and price are among the greatest benefits, and the way in such matters is expansion through the most effective means due to severe need, not restriction. Therefore, the Shafi'i view is not accepted.

This passage thus provides a complete presentation of the dispute: the Shafi'i position with its proof, the Hanafi rebuttal with its own evidence, and the underlying reasoning. The teacher must emphasize that the difference has practical consequences: for example, in the exchange of dates of different qualities, Hanafis consider any excess riba as long as they are the same genus and measure, while Shafi'is only consider it riba if dates are edible (which they are), but they also require equivalence unless the transaction is spot (hand in hand). However, the Hanafi effective cause is more restrictive in some cases (e.g., non-edible weighed items like iron may not be subject to riba in Shafi'i view if not monetary). But the student should focus on understanding the principle difference: the choice of effective cause based on what manifests the property's value.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): An excess in a commutative contract that is devoid of a countervalue and stipulated in the contract (الفضل الخالي عن عوض شرط في العقد).
علة (‘illah): The effective cause that triggers a legal ruling; here it is the attribute that makes riba applicable to an item.
طعم (ṭu‘m): Edibility: anything commonly eaten, whether as food or for pleasure, including fruits, grains, vegetables, and spices.
ثمنية (thamaniyyah): Being a price: items that are inherently prices (gold, silver) or that people agree upon as currency.
مماثلة (mumāthalah): Equivalence between two things in form (measure or weight) and meaning (genus).
قدر مع الجنس (qadr ma‘a al-jins): Quantity with genus: the Hanafi effective cause of riba, meaning the combination of being a measurable/weighable commodity and being of the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effective cause for riba in an exchange?
A) The item being edible (tu‘m)
B) The item being a price (thamaniyyah)
C) The item being measured or weighed and of the same genus (qadr ma‘a al-jins)
D) The item being valuable and having sanctity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines riba by quantity with genus, while the Shafi'i school defines it by edibility or price; the difference affects which transactions are considered ribawi.

Hanafi Proof That Riba's Cause Is Measure and Genus
Establishes Hanafi proof from hadith and rationale for riba condition equality in measure and genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof for the cause of riba and explain why quality is not considered a valid factor.

Core Idea
Equality in measure and genus is the condition for riba; quality is irrelevant by text and custom.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi proof that riba's 'illa is measure and genus. It cites the hadith 'mithlan bi mithlin' to establish equality as a condition in sale, provides three rationales, and dismisses quality and taste as irrelevant. The passage also refutes the Shafi'i consideration of taste, anchoring the Hanafi position that only measure and genus matter in ribawi exchanges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Primary Proof
Locate the hadith reference and understand that the Prophet (peace be upon him) made equality a condition in sale. This is the textual basis for the Hanafi ruling.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim but referred to as 'he made equality a condition'.
2
Understand the Three Rationales
Note the three objectives: (1) to realize the meaning of sale (exchange), (2) to protect people's wealth from loss, (3) to complete the benefit by ensuring mutual delivery. These justify why equality is required.
These are a posteriori justifications, not the primary proof.
3
Define Equality in Form and Meaning
Equality is considered in form (quantity/measure) and meaning (genus). Measure equalizes essence, genus equalizes type. Excess beyond this is riba.
Measure and genus are the two components that define mumathalah.
4
Analyze the Dismissal of Quality
The text gives three reasons: (1) quality is not considered a difference customarily, (2) considering quality would block all transactions, (3) the hadith states 'its good and bad are the same.'
This directly refutes the Shafi'i consideration of taste.
5
Apply to a Practical Scenario
For example, exchanging 1 kg of high-quality dates for 1 kg of low-quality dates is permissible because measure is equal and genus is same. Quality does not affect the ruling.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنا انه أوجب المماثلة شرطا فى البيع وهو المقصود بسوقه تحقيقا لمعنى البيع اذ هو ينبئى عن و ذالك بالتماثل اوصيانة لاموال الناس عن التوى اوتتميما للفائدة باتصال التسليم به ثم يلزم عند قوته حرمة الربواو المماثلة بين الشيأين باعتبار الصورة والمعنى والمعيار يسوى الذات والجنسية تسوي المعنى فيظهر الفضل على ذالك فيتحقق الربوا لان الربوا هو الفضل المستحق لاحد المتعاقدين في المعاوضة الخالي عن عوض شرط فيه ولا يعتبر الوصف لانه لا يعد تفاوتا عرفا اولان في اعتباره سد باب البياعات اولقوله عليه السلام جيدها ورديها سواء والطعم والثمنية من اعظم وجوه المنافع والسبيل في مثلها الطلاق بابلغ الوجوه لشدة الاحتياج اليها دون التضييق فيه فلا معتبر بما ذكره
And we argue that he (the Prophet) made equality a condition in sale, and this is the purpose of its mention, to realize the meaning of sale, for it indicates exchange, and that is through equality, or to protect people's wealth from loss, or to complete the benefit by connecting delivery to it. Then, when it (equality) is lost, the prohibition of riba becomes necessary. Equality between two things is considered in terms of form and meaning. The measure equalizes the essence, and genus equalizes the meaning, so excess appears on that, and riba is realized. For riba is the excess due to one of the two contracting parties in an exchange, devoid of compensation, and stipulated in the contract. And quality is not considered, because it is not regarded as a difference customarily, or because considering it would close the doors of transactions, or due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Its good and bad are the same.' And taste and monetary value are among the greatest aspects of benefit, and the way in such matters is expansion in the most effective ways due to severe need, not restriction. So what he (al-Shafi'i) mentioned is not reliable.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi proof for the cause of riba (riba). The core argument is that the hadith "mithlan bi mithlin" (like for like) establishes equality as a necessary condition in the exchange of ribawi goods. The commentator, in line with Al-Hidayah's original, explains that this equality must be in measure (qadr) and genus (jins). Measure covers form/quantity, while genus covers intrinsic type/quality. The Prophet's command implies that when equality is absent, the excess is riba. Three rationales are given: (1) to fulfill the meaning of exchange (muʿawada), which inherently requires equivalence; (2) to protect people's wealth from loss; (3) to complete the benefit by ensuring mutual delivery. The passage then dismisses the consideration of quality (wasf) or taste (taʿm) on three grounds: custom does not treat quality as a difference; if quality mattered, trade would be impossible because no two items are identical in all attributes; and the hadith explicitly states that good and bad are equal in such transactions. This is a direct refutation of the Shafiʿi position that considers taste as an independent cause. The Hanafi school maintains that only measure (for all ribawi goods) and genus (for staple foods and gold/silver) determine riba, while quality is irrelevant. The authority weight of this ruling is Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is from the base matn of Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
مماثلة (mumathalah): Equality between two things in form (quantity) and meaning (intrinsic type/jins).
قدر (qadr): Numerical quantity determined by standard measures like weight or volume.
جنس (jins): Genus or category of the item, such as wheat, barley, gold, silver.
طعم (ta'm): Taste or edibility/economic benefit as considered by some schools as cause of riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid cause (illa) of riba in the exchange of ribawi goods?
A) The quality (jidad) of the goods
B) The measure (qadr) when the genus (jins) is the same
C) The taste (ta'm) of the goods
D) The customary value of the goods

Key Takeaway
Riba in exchange is caused by inequality in measure when the genus is the same; quality is irrelevant by text and custom.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Three Proofs for the Condition of Tamathul in Ribawi Sales
Ruling with proof and expansion of 'illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rational proofs for tamathul and identify qadr and jins as the necessary elements for equality in Hanafi ribawi sales.

Core Idea
Tamathul in both measure and genus is wajib; any excess without equivalent is riba.

This lesson unpacks three rational proofs from Hanafi jurisprudence that establish equality (tamathul) as a required condition in exchanges of ribawi items. You will see why equality protects property, completes the contract, and is supported by the Prophet's hadith. We also clarify that equality is twofold: formal (by measure) and essential (by genus), and why other proposed causes like edibility are not accepted.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the three proofs
Identify each rational proof: (1) logical exchange requires equality, (2) protects against loss of property, (3) benefit of sale is perfected through mutual possession.
Each proof builds on the idea that excess without countervalue is riba.
2
Connect proofs to the hadith
The proofs point to the hadith 'al-fadlu riba', showing that excess is forbidden, thus requiring equality.
The hadith is used as textual support for the rational arguments.
3
Distinguish formal and essential equality
Formal equality is through measure (qadr); essential equality is through genus (jins). Both are needed for tamathul.
Example: wheat vs barley: equal measure but different genus, so essential equality is lacking.
4
Understand why qadr and jins are the 'illa
Only qadr and jins achieve equality; ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price) do not affect equality, so they are not the cause of riba according to Hanafis.
This is the point of dispute with the Shafi'i school.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is hold that the 'illa of riba is ta'm and thamaniyya. Hanafis reject this because ta'm does not ensure equality.
The practical difference: Hanafis require same genus and measure; Shafi'is require same genus and edibility.

برابر ہے حاصل یہ ہوا کہ حدیث کا مقصد اموال ربویہ کی بیع میں عوضین کے درمیان مماثلت کا شرط ہونا بیان کرنا ہے اور مماثلت ثابت کرنے میں قدر اور جنس مؤثر ہیں کیونکہ مماثلت صوری قدر کے ذریعہ حاصل ہوتی ہے اور مماثلت معنوی جنس کے ذریعہ حاصل ہوتی ہے اس لیے ان دونوں کو ربوا کی علت قرار دیا گیا اور طعم اور حمیت کو مماثلت ثابت کرنے میں چونکہ کوئی دخل نہیں ہے اس لیے ان کو علت ربوا قرار نہیں دیا گیا۔
It can be that the exchange is on the basis of equality and equivalence between the two countervalues. For if one countervalue is more and the other less, then the extra amount in the one that is more has no corresponding countervalue. When that extra amount lacks a countervalue, the meaning of exchange is not realized. When exchange is not realized, the meaning of sale and compensation is not realized. So it is established that to realize the meaning of sale, equality and equivalence between the two countervalues is necessary. The second reason is that equality and equivalence between the two countervalues was made a condition to protect people's property from loss. For if one countervalue is more and the other less, then the extra amount in the larger countervalue—the exchange, i.e., the contract of sale—would cause loss to the party who received the lesser, because he receives nothing in return for that extra amount. When he receives nothing for the extra amount, that extra amount is wasted in his right. So to protect that extra amount from being wasted, equality and equivalence were made a condition in the sale of ribawi items. Pointing to this extra amount, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Al-fadlu riba,' meaning that in Allah's statement 'and Allah has forbidden riba,' riba refers to this excess and increase. The third reason is that the benefit of sale is fully realized when there is equality and equivalence in mutual possession. For the benefit of sale is that the seller becomes owner of one countervalue and the buyer becomes owner of the other. And it is well established that the contract itself establishes ownership of the substance over the countervalues, and the full contract establishes ownership of disposal. The full contract occurs only when the parties take possession of the countervalues. So it is established that the benefit of sale is perfected through possession. When the benefit of sale is perfected through possession, then to perfect the benefit, equality and equivalence in possession is necessary. And equality in possession is that the parties take possession of their respective countervalues. This is indicated by the phrase 'hand to hand'. From these three reasons, it is known that the hadith intends to express the obligation of equality. So if the condition of equality is lost, then the prohibition of riba becomes necessary, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Al-fadlu riba.' And equality between two items is in form and meaning. For every item exists with its form or meaning. So equality between two items is established by form and meaning. And qadr (measure) is the name for equality in measurement, i.e., equality of two things in terms of the standard. So formal equality is attained through measure. And jins (genus) is the name for similarity in meanings, i.e., being similar in meaning. So essential equality is attained through genus. The author of Hidayah says that measure makes two things equal in essence and form, and genus makes them equal in meaning. For example, one kilo of wheat and one kilo of maize are equal in form and measure, so in form, wheat is one kilo and maize is one kilo, but since wheat and maize are not the same genus, equality in meaning is lacking. Similarly, one qiz of wheat and one qafiz of wheat are not equal in form, but one kilo of wheat and one kilo of wheat are equal in both form and meaning. The conclusion is that the hadith aims to state that equality between countervalues is a condition in the sale of ribawi items, and both qadr and jins are effective in establishing equality. For formal equality is attained through qadr, and essential equality through jins. Therefore, both are made the 'illa of riba. As for ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price), since they have no role in establishing equality, they are not made the 'illa of riba.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the commentary of Al-Hidayah. It provides three rational proofs for the condition of tamathul (equality) in ribawi transactions, supported by the hadith 'al-fadlu riba'. The first proof is based on the logic of exchange: if one party gives more, the extra lacks an equivalent, so exchange is not realized. The second proof protects property rights: the extra amount without compensation is wasteful, so equality prevents loss. The third proof concerns possession: the benefit of sale requires mutual possession of equal amounts. The hadith 'al-fadlu riba' confirms that any excess is riba. The passage then distinguishes between formal equality (through qadr/measure) and essential equality (through jins/genus). Both are required for a valid sale of ribawi items. Ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (monetary value) are not considered because they do not affect equality. This establishes the Hanafi position that the 'illa of riba is qadr and jins jointly, not ta'm alone as held by the Shafi'i school.

Key Terms
مماثلت (tamathul): Equality, equivalence between two items in both form (measure) and meaning (genus).
قدر (qadr): Measure, criterion of quantity (e.g., weight, volume, length) used for formal equality.
جنس (jins): Genus, category of the item (e.g., wheat, barley) used for essential equality.
علت ('illa): The effective cause or legal rationale for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what are the two necessary elements for equality (tamathul) in a ribawi sale?
A) Measure (qadr) and price (thamaniyya)
B) Measure (qadr) and genus (jins)
C) Edibility (ta'm) and price (thamaniyya)
D) Genus (jins) and quality (wasf)

Key Takeaway
Equality in both measure and genus is wajib in ribawi sales; any excess without equivalent is riba, as confirmed by the three proofs and hadith.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

Why Quality Is Not Considered in Ribawi Equality
Explains why wasf is excluded from the riba condition with three answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not consider quality (wasf) in establishing equality in ribawi transactions, and state the three answers from Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Quality differences in ribawi goods do not create riba — only measure and genus matter.

The passage addresses a key question: if equality in ribawi transactions requires matching in measure and genus, why is quality not also required? The Hanafi school offers three answers. This lesson unpacks those answers and explores the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling on excess (tafadul)
The passage first establishes that any stipulated excess in same genus and measure is riba. The example of 1 qafiz for 2 qafiz illustrates prohibited riba, while a voluntary gift after the contract is not.
Riba is defined as a stipulated excess in an exchange contract.
2
Identify the question about wasf
Why is quality not considered in establishing equality? The passage poses this question because equality could also be through quality.
3
Analyze the three answers
Examine each answer: (1) 'urf 'amm (common custom) ignores quality differences — al-Khadim objects that prices vary with quality. (2) If quality mattered, ribawi transactions would become impossible because no two items are exactly alike. (3) A hadith states that good and bad are equal in ribawi items.
The hadith 'jayyiduha wa radiyuha sawa' is the strongest proof.
4
Reflect on the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school relies on the second and third answers over the first due to the objection from al-Khadim. The mufta bihi is that quality differences do not affect the riba ruling.
The ruling remains that only measure and genus matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پس جب مماثلت کا شرط ہونا قدر اور جنس سے ثابت ہوا تو تفاضل بھی اسی پر ظاہر ہوگا یعنی قدر اور جنس کے اتحاد کے باوجود اگر کوئی عوض زیادہ ہوا تو یہ فصل اور ربوا کہلائے گا کیونکہ ربوا اسی زیادتی کو کہتے ہیں جو عقد معاوضہ میں احد العاقدین کے لیے حاصل ہو عوض سے خالی ہو اور عقد میں مشروط ہو مثلاً ایک آدمی نے ایک قفیز گندم دو قفیز گندم کے عوض فروخت کیا تو اس میں ایک قفیز گندم چونکہ بلاعوض ایک عاقد کے لیے زائد حاصل ہے اور عقد میں مشروط ہے اس لیے یہ ربوا کہلائے گا۔ اور اگر ایک قفیز گندم ایک قفیز گندم کے عوض بیچا مگر بعد میں احد العاقدین نے اپنے ساتھی کو دو قفیز گندم دیدیئے تو یہ ربوا نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ زیادتی کا عقد کے اندر مشروط ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ولا يعتبر الوصف ...... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ دو چیزوں کے درمیان مماثلت جس طرح قدر اور جنس کے ساتھ متحقق ہوتی ہے اسی طرح وصف کے ساتھ بھی مماثلت ثابت ہوتی ہے لیکن آپ نے مماثلت ثابت کرنے میں قدر اور جنس کا اعتبار تو کیا ہے مگر وصف کا اعتبار نہیں کیا۔ اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ صاحب ہدایہ اس کے تین جواب پیش کرتے ہیں۔ پہلا جواب یہ ہے کہ عرف عام میں چونکہ وصف کے اعتبار سے تفاوت شمار نہیں کیا جاتا اس لیے وصف کا اعتبار نہ ہو گا چنانچہ احد البدلین اگر جید اور آخر ردی ہو تو جودت کے اعتبار سے فضل اور زیادتی معتبر ہوگی یعنی ایک عوض کا جید اور دوسرے کا ردی ہونا ربوا شمار نہ ہو گا۔ اس جواب پر خادم کو ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر عرف عام میں تفاوت فی الوصف معتبر نہ ہوتا تو وصف متفاوت ہونے کی وجہ سے قیمتوں میں فرق نہ ہوتا حالانکہ شیئی جید کی قیمت زیادہ ہوتی ہے اور ردی کی قیمت کم ہوتی ہے پس تفاوت فی الوصف کی وجہ سے قیمتوں میں فرق ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ عرف عام میں وصف کے اعتبار سے تفاوت معتبر ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر وصف کے اعتبار سے تفاوت کا اعتبار کیا گیا تو اموال ربویہ میں خرید و فروخت کے دروازے ہی بند ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ بات ناممکن ہے کہ ایک گندم دوسرے گندم کا من کل وجہ مماثل ہو کچھ نہ کچھ فرق ضرور ہوگا اور اس فرق کی وجہ سے چونکہ ربوا لازم آئے گا اس لیے گویا ان چیزوں کی بیع ہی ناممکن ہے حالانکہ ان چیزوں کی بیع کا دروازہ کھلا ہوا ہے اس لیے ہم نے وصف کے اعتبار سے تفاوت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا۔ تیسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ مدنی آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جیدها و ردیها سواء یعنی اموال ربویہ میں کھرا کھوٹا سب برابر ہے یعنی کھرے اور کھوٹے کے اعتبار سے تفاوت معتبر نہیں ہے۔
So when the condition of equality is established through measure and genus, then excess (tafadul) will also be apparent on this basis: that despite unity of measure and genus, if one countervalue is more, then this is called excess (fadl) and riba. Because riba is the name for that excess which is acquired by one of the two parties in an exchange contract without a countervalue and is stipulated in the contract. For example, if a man sells one qafiz of wheat for two qafiz of wheat, then one qafiz of wheat is acquired by one party without a countervalue and is stipulated in the contract, so this is riba. And if he sells one qafiz of wheat for one qafiz of wheat, but later one party gives his companion two qafiz of wheat, then this is not riba, because it is necessary for the excess to be stipulated in the contract. 'And wasf is not considered...' to the end of the chapter is the answer to a question. The question is: just as equality between two things is established through measure and genus, similarly equality is established through quality. But you have considered measure and genus in establishing equality, but not quality. What is the reason? The author of Al-Hidayah gives three answers. The first answer is that in common custom ('urf 'amm), differences are not considered in terms of quality, so quality is not considered. For example, if one of the two countervalues is good and the other is bad, then the excess and increase in goodness is not considered, i.e., one countervalue being good and the other bad is not considered riba. There is an objection to this answer from al-Khadim: that if differences in quality were not considered in common custom, then there would be no difference in prices due to differing quality, whereas the price of a good item is higher and the price of a bad item is lower. So the difference in prices due to difference in quality proves that differences in quality are considered in common custom. The second answer is that if differences in quality were considered, then the doors of buying and selling of ribawi items would be closed. Because it is impossible for one wheat to be exactly similar to another wheat in every aspect; some difference will necessarily exist. Due to that difference, riba would become necessary, so the sale of such items would be impossible, whereas the door of sale of these items is open. Therefore, we have not considered differences due to quality. The third answer is that the Madani master (peace be upon him) said: 'Its good and its bad are equal,' meaning that in ribawi items, good and bad are all equal, i.e., differences in purity and impurity are not considered.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on tamathul. It first applies the principle to tafadul (excess): if measure and genus are the same, any stipulated excess is riba. The example of one qafiz for two qafiz illustrates prohibited riba, while a voluntary gift after the contract is not. The main discussion addresses why quality (wasf) is not considered in establishing equality. Three answers are given: (1) Custom ('urf 'amm) does not treat quality differences as significant, though al-Khadim objects that prices vary with quality. (2) If quality mattered, ribawi transactions would become impossible because no two items are exactly alike, yet shari'ah permits them. (3) A hadith states that good and bad are equal in ribawi exchange. This establishes the Hanafi view that quality variation does not create riba; only measure and genus count.

Key Terms
وصف (wasf): Quality, attribute of an item (e.g., good, bad, pure, impure).
عرف عام (urf 'amm): Common custom, general practice of the people.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is quality (wasf) not considered in ribawi equality?
A) Because it is impossible to measure quality
B) Because the hadith says good and bad are equal
C) Because quality does not affect price
D) Because measure and genus are sufficient

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that quality (wasf) is not a factor in ribawi transactions; only measure and genus determine riba.

Refutation of Ta'm and Thamaniyya as 'Illa of Riba
Refutes Shafi'i 'illa of riba using rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi refutation of ta'm and thamaniyya as the 'illa of riba and apply the Hanafi position on the 'illa of riba to differentiate rulings.

Core Idea
Necessities cannot be prohibited; thus ta'm and thamaniyya cannot be the 'illa of riba.

Imam Shafi'i argued that the prohibition of riba applies to all edible and monetary items based on the 'illa of ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price). The Hanafi school rejects this, offering a rational argument: both ta'm and thamaniyya are necessities of life, and Allah's divine practice is to expand provisions where need is greatest, not to restrict them. This lesson unpacks that refutation and its implications for defining the true 'illa of riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i position
State clearly that Imam Shafi'i considers ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price/money) as the effective causes ('illa) for the prohibition of riba.
This means riba would be prohibited in all food and all monetary items.
2
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that both ta'm and thamaniyya are essential human needs; life depends on food, and money is needed for transactions. Therefore, prohibiting riba based on these would contradict Allah's practice of expanding access to necessities.
The Hanafi view is that the 'illa is qadr (measure) and jins (genus), not ta'm or thamaniyya.
3
Analyze the rational argument (dalil aqli)
The passage uses qiyas: just as air and water are universally available due to intense need, so too food and money should not be restricted by a broad prohibition. Intense need leads to expansion, not restriction.
This is a logical refutation, not a textual one, hence 'dalil aqli'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Shafi'i would prohibit riba in all edibles and money; Hanafi limits it to items that are both measured (qadr) and same genus (jins), like wheat and barley, or gold and silver.
This affects which transactions are considered ribawi.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi school considers its position stronger because it harmonises with divine practice and avoids excessive restrictions on necessities.
The tarjih is based on both aqli (rational) and naqli (hadith) evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطعم والثمنية .... الخ سے امام شافعی کی بیان کردہ علت ربوا کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ طعم اور ثمنیت کو حرمت ربوا کی علت قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کے ساتھ بڑے بڑے منافع متعلق ہیں چنانچہ طعم پر انسان کی زندگی موقوف ہے اور ثمنیت ضروریات زندگی حاصل کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے گویا انسان کو ان دونوں کی طرف شدتِ احتیاج ہوتی ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی عادت ہے کہ انسان جس چیز کی طرف زیادہ محتاج ہوتا ہے اس میں اسی درجہ کا توسعہ کرتا ہے چنانچہ ہوا اور پانی کی طرف شدت احتیاج کی وجہ سے ان کو عام سے عام تر کر دیا گیا ہے یہ دونوں چیزیں ہر آدمی کو بآسانی حاصل ہو جاتی ہیں بلکہ بسا اوقات شدت احتیاج حرام کو
The section 'and edibility and price...' to the end is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's stated 'illa of riba. The summary of the answer is that making ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price) the 'illa of the prohibition of riba is not correct, because both are associated with great benefits. Indeed, human life depends on ta'm (food), and thamaniyya (price/money) is the means to obtain the necessities of life. In other words, humans have intense need for both. And Allah's practice is that the more need humans have for something, the more He grants expansion in it. Thus, due to intense need for air and water, they have been made universally available; these two things are easily obtained by every person. In fact, sometimes intense need makes the forbidden...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhab dispute. Imam Shafi'i holds that the 'illa (effective cause) for the prohibition of riba is ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (price/money). The Hanafi response, as stated in Al-Hidayah, refutes this by noting that both ta'm and thamaniyya are necessities of life. Since Allah expands provisions for things most needed (like air and water), making them generally available, the Hanafi school argues that imposing a prohibition on them would contradict this divine practice. Therefore, they cannot be the 'illa. This aligns with the Hanafi view that the 'illa is qadr and jins together. The text ends abruptly, but the argument suggests that if ta'm and thamaniyya were the 'illa, riba would be prohibited in all food and money, which would be impractical given their necessity.

Key Terms
طعم (ta'm): Edibility, the property of being food.
ثمنیت (thamaniyya): Price, monetary value, the property of being used as a medium of exchange.
علة ('illa): Effective cause; the attribute that renders a legal ruling applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ta'm (edibility) not a valid 'illa for the prohibition of riba?
A) Because edibility is not a common attribute among ribawi items.
B) Because human life depends on food, so Allah expands its access.
C) Because the hadith does not mention edibility at all.
D) Because edibility is a valid 'illa only for non-ribawi items.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school refutes ta'm and thamaniyya as the 'illa of riba by arguing that necessities are expanded by Allah, not restricted, thus the 'illa must be qadr and jins.

The Effective Cause of Riba in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines riba, condition of mumathalah, three answers for ignoring wasf, refutes Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the 'illa of riba, distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, and apply the three proofs for ignoring wasf.

Core Idea
Riba is defined by stipulated excess in the same kind and measure; quality differences are irrelevant.

Riba is a central prohibition in Islamic finance, but what exactly makes an exchange ribawi? This passage from al-Hidayah lays out the Hanafi position with clarity: the effective cause ('illa) is a combination of kind (jins) and measure (qadr). Quality (wasf) is deliberately excluded. The author not only defines riba but also provides three compelling reasons for ignoring quality differences, and then refutes the Shafi'i school's alternative 'illa of edibility and monetary value. By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi school takes a broader view than others, and how this impacts real transactions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the 'illa of riba
Identify the two components: kind (jins) and quantity (qadr). Note that quality (wasf) is not considered. Understand the definition of riba as stipulated excess without compensation.
The Hanafi 'illa is broader than the Shafi'i, covering all measured and weighed items of the same kind.
2
Examine the three reasons for ignoring wasf
First, custom disregards quality differences in ribawi exchanges. Second, considering wasf would block all sales because perfect equality is impossible. Third, the hadith 'jīduhā wa radiyuhā sawā' explicitly states equality of good and bad.
The commentator raises an objection to the first reason, but the second and third are stronger.
3
Understand the Shafi'i alternative 'illa
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the 'illa for foodstuffs is ta'm (edibility) and for gold and silver is thamaniyya (monetary value). This restricts riba to those categories.
The Hanafi school responds by arguing that these are necessities where the law grants ease, not restriction.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i view
The Hanafi response demonstrates that making ta'm and thamaniyya the 'illa would impose hardship, contradicting the principle that severe need leads to expansion (like air and water, and permissibility of carrion in necessity).
This is a rational argument based on the maqasid of the Shari'ah.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under the Hanafi view, riba applies to all items measured by volume or weight (makyūlāt and mawzūnāt) of the same kind, not just food and precious metals. For example, exchanging different quantities of iron is riba for Hanafi but not for Shafi'i.
Understanding this difference is crucial for fatwa and practice.

Source Text

قراردینا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کے ساتھ بڑے بڑے منافع متعلق ہیں چنا نچہ طعم پر انسان کی زندگی موقوف ہے اور منیت ضروریات زندگی حاصل کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے گویا انسان کو ان دونوں کی طرف شدتِ احتیاج ہوتی ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی عادت ہے کہ انسان جس چیز کی طرف زیادہ محتاج ہوتا ہے اس میں اسی درجہ کا توسیع ہوتا ہے چنانچہ ہوا اور پانی کی طرف شدت احتیاج کی وجہ سے ان کو عام سے عام تر کر دیا گیا ہے یہ دونوں چیزیں ہر آدمی کو بآسانی حاصل ہو جاتی ہیں بلکہ بسا اوقات شدت احتیاج حرام کو حلال کر دیتی ہے جیسا کہ حالت اضطرار میں مردار اور سور کے کھانے کی اجازت ہے پس طعم اور میت کی طرف کثرت احتیاج کا ہونا اس بات کا متقاضی ہے کہ ان میں زیادہ سے زیادہ توسیع کیا جائے نہ یہ کہ ان میں تنگی کی جائے اور ان کو حرمت ربوا کی علت قرار دینے میں سراسر تنگی ہے اس لیے ان کو حرمت ربوا کی علت قرار دینا مناسب نہ ہوگا اور امام شافعی نے جو کچھ ذکر کیا اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary volume eight, 295: ...since they have no involvement, they are not made the cause of riba. The Book of Sales. Then when it is established that the condition of similarity is in quantity and kind, then excess also becomes apparent. i.e., despite unity of quantity and kind, if one counter-value is more, it is called fadl and riba, because riba is the excess that is obtained for one of the two contracting parties in a commutative contract without compensation and stipulated in the contract. For example, a man sells one qafiz of wheat for two qafiz of wheat: here, one qafiz of wheat is obtained without compensation for one party and is stipulated in the contract, so it is called riba. And if he sold one qafiz of wheat for one qafiz of wheat, but later one of the parties gave his companion two qafiz of wheat, then... The stipulation of excess in the contract is necessary for riba. 'And description is not considered...' etc. This is an answer to a question. The question is: similarity between two things is established both by quantity and kind as well as by description, but you have considered quantity and kind for establishing similarity, not description. What is the reason? The author of Hidayah gives three answers. The first answer: because in common custom, difference in description is not counted, so description is not considered. For example, if one counter-value is good and the other is bad, then the surplus due to goodness is not considered; i.e., one good and the other bad is not counted as riba. The commentator (khadim) has an objection: if difference in description were not considered in custom, then there would be no price difference due to differing descriptions, whereas the price of a good thing is higher and of a bad thing lower. So price difference due to difference in description proves that difference in description is considered in custom. The second answer: if difference in description were considered, then the door of buying and selling ribawi goods would be closed, because it is impossible for one wheat to be exactly similar to another in every respect; there will always be some difference, and due to that difference riba would become necessary, so the sale of these goods would be impossible, whereas the door of their sale is open; therefore we did not consider difference due to description. The third answer: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Its good and its bad are equal,' i.e., in ribawi goods, good and bad are equal; difference due to goodness or badness is not considered. As for 'edibility (ta'm) and monetary value (thamaniyya)' etc., this is an answer to the cause of riba stated by Imam Shafi'i. The gist of the answer: making ta'm and thamaniyya the cause of prohibition of riba is not correct, because great benefits are attached to both: human life depends on ta'm, and thamaniyya is a means of obtaining necessities of life; man has severe need of both, and Allah's custom is that the more a thing is needed, the more expansion is made in it. Thus, due to severe need for air and water, they have been made most common; these two things are easily available to everyone. Sometimes severe need makes the forbidden lawful, as in case of necessity eating carrion and pork is permitted. So the severe need for ta'm and thamaniyya demands that expansion be made in them to the maximum, not restriction. Making them the cause of riba is nothing but restriction, so it is not appropriate to make them the cause of riba. And what Imam Shafi'i mentioned is not reliable.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author first defines riba as stipulated excess in a commutative contract without compensation. He establishes that the condition of similarity (mumathala) is in quantity (qadr) and kind (jins), not in description (wasf). Then he answers why description is ignored: first, because custom disregards it; second, considering it would block all sales; third, the hadith 'jīduhā wa radiyuhā sawā' (the good and the bad are equal) supports it. Finally, he refutes Imam Shafi'i's 'illa of ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (monetary value) by arguing that these are necessities where the Shari'ah grants ease, not restriction, so they cannot be the cause of prohibition.

Key Terms
ربوا (ribā): Prohibited excess in exchange, defined as any stipulated increase in one counter-value without compensation.
مماثلت (mumāthalah): Equality in standard measure (kayl or wazn) between items of the same kind.
قدر (qadr): Quantity measured by standard measure (kayl or wazn). One of the two components of the 'illa for riba.
جنس (jins): Kind or species. Second component of the 'illa for riba.
وصف (waṣf): Quality or attribute (e.g., good vs. bad). Not considered in mumāthala for ribawi items.
طعم (ṭa'm): Nourishment or edibility. According to Shafi'i, the 'illa for riba in foodstuffs.
ثمنية (thamaniyya): Monetary value or being a medium of exchange. Shafi'i uses it as 'illa for gold and silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following correctly identifies the effective cause ('illa) for the prohibition of riba?
A) Qadr (measure) and jins (kind)
B) Ta'm (edibility) and thamaniyya (monetary value)
C) Wasf (quality) and qadr (measure)
D) The necessity of the items exchanged

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi 'illa for riba is quantity and kind; quality is irrelevant due to the hadith, custom, and practical necessity.
