كتاب البيوع
أشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم
چیزیں وزن میں صورت اور معنی اور حکم کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہوں تو وزن ان کو من کل وجہ جامع نہ ہوگا پس وزن کے اندر شبہ کو شبہ اللہ کی طرف اتار لیا جائے گا اور شبہ الشبہ غیر معتبر ہے۔
تشریح یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک علت ربا دو چیزیں ہیں ایک قدر دوم جنس عقلی طور پر اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ یا دونوں موجود ہوں گی یا دونوں معدوم ہوں گی یا ایک موجود اور ایک معدوم ہوگی اگر دونوں چیزیں موجود ہوں تو سابق میں گذر چکا کہ اس صورت میں تفاضل اور نساء دونوں حرام ہوں گے یعنی احد البد لین کا کم اور دوسرے کا زیادہ ہونا بھی حرام ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں حرمت ربوا کی علت نہیں پائی گئی ہے اور بیع کے اندر اصل اباحت ہے چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے احل الله البیع پس جب اباحت اصل ہے اور حرمت کی علت موجود نہیں ہے تو یہ بیع حلال ہوگی خواہ تفاضل کے ساتھ ہو یا بغیر تفاضل کے ، ادھار ہو یا نقد بہر صورت جائز ہے اور اگر ایک وصف موجود ہو اور ایک معدوم ہو تو تفاضل حلال ہوگا اور ادھار حرام ہوگا ۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے ایک ہروی تھان دو ہروی تھانوں کے عوض بیعا تو اس صورت میں جنس تو پائی گئی کیونکہ دونوں عوضوں کی ایک ہی جنس ہے لیکن قدر نہیں پایا گیا کیونکہ کپڑا نہ مکیلات میں سے ہے اور نہ موزونات میں سے ہے بلکہ مزروعات میں سے ہے پس ایک تھان کا دو تھانوں کے عوض بیچنا تو جائز ہے مگر ایک تھان کا ایک تھان کے عوض ادھار بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر گندم کو جو کے عوض بیعا تو اس صورت میں قدر تو موجود ہے لیکن جنس موجود نہیں ہے جنس کا موجود نہ ہونا تو ظاہر ہے اور قدر اس لیے موجود ہے کہ دونوں عوض مکیلات میں سے ہیں پس گندم کی بیع جو کے عوض کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ تو جائز ہے لیکن ادھار جائز نہیں ہے حاصل یہ ہوا کہ زیادتی ربوا کا حرام ہونا دو وصف کے ساتھ ہے اور ادھار کا حرام ہونا ایک وصف کے ساتھ ہے حضرت امام شافعی کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ تنہا جنس ادھار کو حرام نہیں کرتی ہے یعنی اگر دونوں عوضوں کی جنس ایک ہوا اور ظلم یا ثمنیت نہ ہو تو ان کے نزدیک ادھار بھی حرام نہ ہوگا۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایک عوض کا نقد اور ایک کا ادھار ہونا زیادہ سے زیادہ زیادتی کا شبہ پیدا کرتا ہے کیونکہ نسیئة ( ادھار ) نام ہے مطالبہ کو مؤخر کرنے کا اور مطالبہ کو مؤخر کرنا حقیقتا زیادتی نہیں ہے کیونکہ مطالبہ مؤخر کرنے میں حکما مالیت متفاوت ہوتی ہے حقیقتاً متفاوت نہیں ہوتی۔ پس جب تاخیر مطالبہ سے زیادتی کا شبہ ثابت ہوا نہ کہ حقیقت زیادتی ۔ اور صرف جنس موجود ہونے کی صورت میں حقیقت زیادتی جواز بیع کو منع نہیں کرتی ہے چنانچہ ایک ہروی تھان کا دوہروی تھان کے عوض بیچنا جائز ہے تو شبیہ زیادتی یعنی ایک عوض کا نقد اور ایک عوض کا ادھار ہونا بدرجہ اولی جواز بیع کو منع نہیں کرے گا صاحب عنایہ اور علامہ عینی نے فرمایا کہ امام شافعی کا مذہب بیان کرتے ہوئے خاص طور پر جنس کا ذکر کرنے میں کوئی خاص فائدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک اگر فقط قدر موجود ہو اور جنس موجود نہ ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی ادھار جائز ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے ایک من لوہا ایک من لوہے یا رانگ کے عوض یا ایک من سے زائد کے عوض ادھار بیعا یعنی بیع سلم کی تو ان کے نزدیک جائز ہے حاصل یہ ہوا کہ قدر یا جنس کوئی ایک وصف نساء ( ادھار ) کو حرام نہیں کرتا گویا امام شافعی حرمت نساء کا بالکل انکار کرتے ہیں۔
سوال لیکن یہاں ایک سوال ہوسکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر کسی نے سونا چاندی کے عوض ادھار بیعا یا گندم جو کے عوض ادھار بیعا تو یہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے حالانکہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں محض قدر موجود ہے کیونکہ سونا اور چاندی وہ تو موزونی ہیں اور گندم اور جو دونوں مکیلی ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قدر موجود ہونے کی صورت میں ادھار امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھی حرام ہے حالانکہ پہلے گزر چکا کہ امام شافعی حرمت نساء کا بالکلیہ انکار کرتے ہیں خواہ جنس موجود ہو خواہ قدر موجود ہو۔
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سونے کو چاندی کے عوض اور گندم کو جو کے عوض ادھار بیچنا اس لئے ناجائز نہیں ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک نساء ( ادھار ) حرام ہے بلکہ اس لیے نا جائز ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک بیع صرف اور بیع طعام میں مجلس کے اندر باہم قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور سونے کو چاندی کے عوض بیچنا بیع صرف ہے اور گندم کو جو کے عوض بیچنا بیع طعام ہے اور مجلس کے اندر تقابض اسی وقت ممکن ہے جبکہ بیع ادھار نہ ہو بلکہ نقد ہو ۔ واضح ہو کہ بیع صرف میں مجلس کے اندر باہم قبضہ کرنا ہمارے نزدیک بھی ضروری ہے بہرحال حاصل یہ ہوا کہ تنہاء جنس یا تنہا قدر امام شافعی کے نزدیک ادھار کو حرام نہیں کرتا ہے اس کی تائید حدیث سے بھی ہوتی ہے عن ابن عمر انه جهز جيشاً فأمرني ان اشترى بعبراً ببغیر بن الى اجل ابن عمرؓ سے روایت ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک لشکر تیار کیا اور مجھ کو ایک اونٹنی دو اونٹنیوں کے عوض ادھار یعنی بیع سلم کے طور پر خریدنے کا حکم دیا اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ حضرت علی نے ایک اونٹ ہیں اونٹوں کے عوض ادھار بیعا فتح القدیر) ان روایتوں سے بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ محض جنس کا موجود ہونا نساء یعنی ادھار کو حرام نہیں کرتا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باب ربوا میں ایک حقیقت ربوا ہوتی ہے اور ایک شبہة الربوا ہوتا ہے اور ربوا کا شبہ جب ربوا کی حقیقت سے الگ ہو کر پایا جائے تو وہ ایک محل پحتاج ہوتا ہے اور ایک علت کا محتاج ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ حقیقت ربوا ان دونوں کی محتاج ہوتی ہے اور یہ ممکن نہیں ہے کہ شبہة الربوا کا محل اور اس کی علت وہی ہو جو حقیقت ربوا کا محل اور علت ہے کیونکہ اگر ایسا ہوا تو شبہة الربوا، شبہة الربوا نہ رہے گا بلکہ حقیقت ربوا ہو جائے گا حقیقت ربوا کے مقارن ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ خلاف مفروض ہے اس لیے شبہة الربوا کے واسطے شبہ محل اور شبہ علت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور وہ بیع جس میں نساء ( ادھار ) حرام ہے اس میں عوضین من وجہ مال ربوا ہیں کیونکہ عوضین میں یا تو اتحاد قدر ہو گا جیسا کہ گندم کی بیع جو کے عوض یا اتحاد جنس ہو گا جیسا کہ ہروی کپڑے کی بیع ہروی کپڑے کے عوض اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ ربوا کی علت کا نصاب دو وصف یعنی قدر اور جنس کا مجموعہ ہے اس لیے ان میں سے ایک ربوا کی علت نہیں ہو سکتا۔ البتہ شبہة العلت ہو سکتا ہے اور شبہة العلت سے شبہ الحکم یعنی شبہة الربوا ثابت ہوتا ہے حقیقت ربوا ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ پس جب ایک عوض نقد ہوا اور ایک عوض ادھار ہو تو نقد ہونا مالیت میں زیادتی پیدا کرتا ہے جیسا کہ النقد خير من النسبة مقولہ سے واضح ہے تو نقد ہونے سے اس محل یعنی نقد عوض میں ربوا کا شبہ پیدا کر دیا ہے اور شبہة الربوا جواز بیع سے اسی طرح مانع ہے جس طرح حقیقت ربوا مانع ہے کیونکہ رسول خدا نے ربوا اور ربیبہ (شبہة الربوا) دونوں سے منع فرمایا ہے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ احد الوصفین یعنی قدر یا جنس کا موجود ہونا نساء (ادھار ) کو حرام کر دیتا ہے اسی شبہة الربوا کی وجہ سے اموال ربویہ کو اندازہ سے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے مثلاً ایک آدمی نے گندم کی ایک ڈھیری گندم کی دوسری ایک ڈھیری کے عوض اندازہ سے فروخت کی اور یہ دونوں ڈھیریاں دیکھنے میں برابر ہیں تب بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں زیادتی کا شبہ ہے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ شبہة الربوا جواز بیع سے مانع ہے بلکہ امام زفر کے علاوہ فقہاء احناف نے تو یہاں تک کہا ہے کہ اگر گندم کی ایک ڈھیری ، دوسری ڈھیری کے عوض اندازے سے بیچی پھر دونوں ڈھیریوں کو کیل کیا گیا اور دونوں برابر ہوئیں تو بھی ہمارے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے احد الوصفین کے موجود ہونے کی صورت میں نساء ( ادھار ) حرام ہونے پر احادیث سے بھی استدلال کیا گیا ہے چنانچہ عبادہ بن صامت کی حدیث ربوا کے آخر میں فاذا اختلفت هذه الاصناف فبيعوا كيف شئتم بعد ان يكون يداً بيد ۔ یعنی جب مذکورہ چھ چیزوں کی جنس مختلف ہو جائے تو جس طرح چاہے فروخت کرے بعد اس کے با ہمی قبضہ ہو جائے ۔
Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary on Hidayah Volume 8. If items differ in form, meaning, and ruling in terms of weight, then weight does not encompass them from all aspects, so within weight the doubt is taken to the doubt of Allah, and the doubt of the doubt is not considered. Explanation: It has been established that in our view the cause of riba is two things: measure (qadr) and genus (jins). In rational terms, there are three scenarios: either both are present, both are absent, or one is present and one is absent. If both are present, it has passed before that in that case excess (fadl) and credit (nasi'ah) are both prohibited. If both are absent, then the sale is permissible because prohibition does not apply, as Allah says, 'Allah has permitted trade.' So when permissibility is the principle and the cause of prohibition is not found, this sale is lawful whether with excess or without, credit or cash. And if one attribute is present and one absent, then excess is lawful and credit is prohibited. For example, if a person sells one piece of Herati cloth for two pieces of Herati cloth, then genus is present because both items are of the same genus, but measure is not present because cloth is not among things measured by capacity or weight but among things counted. So selling one piece for two pieces is permissible, but selling one piece for one piece on credit is not permissible. And if wheat is sold for barley, then measure is present but genus is not; the absence of genus is obvious, and measure is present because both are among things measured by capacity. So selling wheat for barley with excess is permissible, but on credit it is not permissible. The conclusion is that the prohibition of excess riba is with two attributes, and the prohibition of credit is with one attribute. Imam al-Shafi'i's school is that genus alone does not prohibit credit, meaning if the genus of both items is the same and they are not monetary or foodstuff, then according to him credit is not prohibited. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that one item being cash and the other credit creates at most a doubt of excess, because nasi'ah is the name for deferring demand, and deferring demand is not in reality excess, because in deferring demand, value differs in a legal sense, not in reality. So when the doubt of excess is established from delay, not the reality of excess. And when only genus is present, the reality of excess does not prevent permissibility of sale; just as selling one Herati cloth for two Herati cloths is permissible, so the semblance of excess, i.e., one item being cash and the other credit, would a fortiori not prevent permissibility of sale. The authors of al-‘Inayah and ‘Allamah al-‘Ayni said that in stating Imam al-Shafi'i's school, specifically mentioning genus has no particular benefit, because according to Imam al-Shafi'i, if only measure is present and genus is not, then the same ruling applies, i.e., credit is permissible. For example, if someone sells one maund of iron for one maund of lead or tin, or for more than one maund on credit (i.e., a salam sale), it is permissible according to him. The conclusion is that measure or genus alone does not prohibit credit; it is as if Imam al-Shafi'i completely denies the prohibition of credit. Question: But here a question may arise: If someone sells gold for silver on credit, or wheat for barley on credit, this is impermissible according to Imam al-Shafi'i, even though in both cases only measure is present, because gold and silver are both weighed, and wheat and barley are both measured. From this it appears that when measure is present, credit is prohibited according to Imam al-Shafi'i, even though it has passed before that Imam al-Shafi'i completely denies the prohibition of credit, whether genus is present or measure. Answer: The answer is that selling gold for silver and wheat for barley on credit is not impermissible because according to them credit is prohibited; rather it is impermissible because according to them in a currency exchange (sarf) transaction and a food transaction, mutual possession in the session is a condition. And selling gold for silver is a sarf transaction, and selling wheat for barley is a food transaction, and mutual possession in the session is only possible when the sale is not on credit but spot. It is clear that in sarf, mutual possession in the session is also necessary in our view. In any case, the conclusion is that genus alone or measure alone does not prohibit credit according to Imam al-Shafi'i. This is also supported by a hadith from Ibn ‘Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prepared an army and ordered me to buy a camel for two camels on credit (i.e., as a salam sale). And in another narration, ‘Ali sold a camel for many camels on credit (as in Fath al-Qadir). These narrations also prove that mere presence of genus does not prohibit credit. Our proof is that in the chapter of riba, there is a reality of riba and a shubhah (doubt/resemblance) of riba. And the doubt of riba, when found separate from the reality of riba, needs a different subject and a different cause, just as the reality of riba needs both. It is not possible that the subject and cause of the shubhah are the same as the subject and cause of the reality of riba, because if so, the shubhah would not remain a shubhah but would become reality or a concomitant of reality, contrary to assumption. Therefore, for the shubhah there must be a doubtful subject and doubtful cause. And the sale in which credit is prohibited, the two countervalues are in some respect ribawi goods, because the two countervalues either have unity of measure (as in wheat for barley) or unity of genus (as in Herati cloth for Herati cloth). It is established that the complete cause of riba consists of two attributes: measure and genus. So one of them cannot be the cause of riba; rather it can be a shubhah cause. And from the shubhah cause, the shubhah ruling (i.e., shubhah of riba) is established, not the reality. So when one item is cash and the other is on credit, being cash creates an increase in value, as the saying 'Cash is better than credit' makes clear. So being cash creates in that subject (the cash item) a shubhah of riba. And the shubhah of riba prevents the permissibility of sale just as the reality of riba prevents it, because the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) forbade both riba and riba-suspicion (shubhah). Thus it is established that the presence of one attribute, measure or genus, prohibits credit. It is due to this shubhah of riba that it is not permissible to sell ribawi goods by estimation. For example, if a person sells one heap of wheat for another heap of wheat by estimation, even if the two heaps appear equal in size, it is not permissible, because there is a doubt of excess. This also shows that the shubhah of riba prevents permissibility of sale. Rather, the Hanafi jurists, except Imam Zufar, have said that even if a heap of wheat is sold for another heap by estimation, then both heaps are measured and found equal, it is still not permissible in our view. On the prohibition of credit when one attribute is present, hadiths are also cited. For example, the hadith of ‘Ubadah ibn Samit at the end of the riba hadith: “But if these categories differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand to hand.” That is, when the genus of the six mentioned items differs, then you may sell however you wish after mutual possession occurs.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the prohibition of credit (nasi'ah) in exchange contracts involving ribawi goods. The Hanafi position is that the effective cause (‘illah) of riba consists of two attributes: genus (jins) and measure (qadr, including both weight and capacity). When both are present (same genus and same measure), both excess (fadl) and credit are prohibited. When both are absent (different genus and different measure, and not monetary or food), the sale is entirely permissible. When only one attribute is present (either same genus with different measure, or same measure with different genus), excess is permissible but credit is prohibited. The Shafi'i school holds that genus alone does not prohibit credit; they deny the prohibition of credit (riba al-nasi'ah) altogether in such cases. Their argument is that credit creates only a doubt (shubhah) of excess, not actual excess, so it should not prohibit the sale. The Hanafi response explains that credit creates a shubhah of riba because cash payment increases value over credit, and this shubhah is treated like actual riba in prohibition, based on the Prophet's prohibition of both riba and its semblance. The passage also addresses a potential objection: if both measure and genus are absent but one item is cash and the other credit, credit is prohibited because the cash item's nature creates a shubhah of riba. The text further mentions that selling ribawi goods by estimation (without exact measurement) is prohibited due to this shubhah, and even if later measured equal, it remains impermissible except according to Imam Zufar. Finally, the hadith of ‘Ubadah ibn Samit is cited to show that when genera differ, hand-to-hand delivery is required, implying that when genera are the same, delayed delivery is prohibited. This passage is an expansion probe from the Hidayah commentary, clarifying the Hanafi stance and refuting the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
ربا (ribā): Illegal increase in exchange contracts, including both excess (fadl) and credit (nasi'ah).
جنس (jins): Genus or category of an item; in riba, it refers to the shared nature of the two countervalues (e.g., both wheat).
قدر (qadr): Measure, including both weight (wazn) and capacity (kayl) as standard units of measurement for ribawi goods.
نسيئة (nasī'ah): Deferred payment or credit sale; one of the two forms of riba (riba al-nasi'ah).
شبهة الربوا (shubhat al-ribā): A doubt or resemblance to riba; a situation that is not actual riba but carries a suspicion of it, rendering the transaction prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone sells one kilogram of wheat for two kilograms of barley to be delivered later, what is the ruling?
A) Permissible because the genera differ.
B) Not permissible because measure (qadr) is shared, so credit (nasi'ah) is prohibited.
C) Permissible because excess is present and that is allowed when genera differ.
D) Not permissible because both genera differ and measure differs.

Key Takeaway
Credit (nasi'ah) in exchanges of ribawi goods is prohibited by the Hanafi school whenever at least one of the two attributes of the 'illah (jins or qadr) is present, due to the principle that a shubhah of riba is treated as actual riba.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
15 min
The Hanafi Prohibition of Nasi'ah with One Attribute: Inter-Madhhab Analysis
Hanafi proof that nasi'ah is haram if jins or qadr exists, with Shafi'i refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits nasi'ah when either genus or measure alone exists, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of shubhat al-riba.

Core Idea
Nasi'ah is haram when even one ribawi attribute exists — shubhat al-riba carries the same prohibition as actual riba.

This lesson unpacks a key inter-madhhab dispute: does credit (nasi'ah) become prohibited in a ribawi exchange when only one of the two attributes (genus or measure) is present? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on the principle of shubhat al-riba, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts the prohibition to cases where both attributes exist or in specific contracts like sarf. We will examine the textual proofs and rational arguments from both sides, then see how the Hanafi response is constructed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
State the exact legal question: Is nasi'ah prohibited when only jins (genus) or only qadr (measure) exists in a ribawi exchange? Note that both schools agree on prohibition when both attributes exist (riba al-fadl).
The dispute is about the intermediate case where only one attribute is present.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that nasi'ah is not prohibited when only one attribute exists. He cites hadith of Ibn Umar and Ali selling camels on credit (genus alone) as evidence. For Shafi'is, hand-to-hand possession is required only in sarf and food-for-food sales by analogy to riba al-fadl.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that nasi'ah is prohibited when either attribute exists. Their proof: hadith of 'Ubadah (hand-to-hand when categories differ), hadith of Abu Dawud (wheat for barley hand-to-hand permitted, credit not), hadith of Samurah (animals for animals credit prohibited). Rational: shubhat al-riba arises from one attribute; the Prophet prohibited riba and its semblance.
Also note the exception: salam for saffron/cotton is allowed despite measure in both.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i proofs
The Hanafis give two responses to the Ibn Umar and Ali hadith: (1) When texts conflict, prohibition takes precedence over permission. (2) Those hadiths are from before the prohibition of riba (mansukh), while the Hanafi proof-texts are later. This resolves the apparent contradiction.
The second response is stronger because it abrogates the earlier permission.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: For Hanafis, selling wheat for barley on credit is haram; for Shafi'is, it is permissible (unless it qualifies as bay' al-ta'am requiring hand-to-hand). Similarly, selling animals of different types on credit is haram for Hanafis but permissible for Shafi'is.
This affects everyday transactions, especially in agricultural and livestock sales.

كتاب البيوع
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ہشتم ملاحظہ فرمائیے اس حدیث میں اختلاف جنس کے وقت کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کرنے کی اجازت تو دی ہے لیکن با ہمی قبضہ کو لازم کرنا ہی تحریم نسیئہ ہے یعنی جب عوضین پر قبضہ لازم ہو گیا تو نساء ( ادھار ) حرام ہو گیا۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ احد الوصفین یعنی قدر کے موجود ہونے کی صورت میں نساء حرام ہے اور ابو داؤد کی روایت ہے لابأس ببيع البر با لشعير و الشعير اكثر هما يدا بيد واما النسيئة فلا یعنی گندم کا جو کے عوض ہاتھ درہاتھ بیچنے میں درانحالیکہ جو زیادہ ہوں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور رہا نسیہ ( ادھار ) تو وہ جائز نہیں ہے اس روایت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اگر قدر موجود ہو اور جنس موجود نہ ہو تو نساء حرام ہے۔ نیز ابوداؤ دہی میں حضرت سمرہ کی روایت ہے عن النبي نهي عن بيع الحيوان با لحيوان نسيئة یعنی رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حیوان کو حیوان کے عوض ادھار بیچنے سے منع کیا ہے۔ اس روایت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جنس موجود ہونے اور قدر موجود نہ ہونے کی صورت میں بھی نساء ( ادھار ) حرام ہے۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب ... امام شافعی کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث ابن عمر اور حدیث علی کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ابن عمر اور حضرت علی کی روایتیں احد الوصفین یعنی جنس موجود ہونے کے باوجود نساء کو مباح کرتی ہیں۔ اور ہماری طرف سے پیش کردہ نساء ( ادھار ) کو
روایتیں
حرام کرتی ہیں اور قاعدہ ہے کہ محرم اور بیچ میں تعارض کے وقت محرم کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے اس لیے ہماری طرف سے پیش کردہ روایتیں راجح
ہوں گی۔
دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث ابن عمر اور حدیث علی تحریم ربوا سے پہلی ہیں اور ہم نے جو روایتیں بیان کی ہیں وہ سب تحریم ربوا سے بعد کی ہیں اس جواب کے بعد بھی کوئی تعارض واقع نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ کا قول الا انه اذا اسلم النقود في الزعفران صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت فاذا او جد أحد هما وعدم الآخر حل التفاضل و حرم النساء سے مستثنیٰ کیا گیا ہے یعنی سابق میں گذرا ہے کہ اگر قدریا جنس ایک وصف موجود ہو اور ایک معدوم ہو تو تفاضل حلال اور نساء حرام ہوتا ہے لیکن ایک صورت اس سے مستثنیٰ ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر نفود یعنی سونا یا چاندی ، زعفران یا اس کے مانند روئی اور لو ہا وغیرہ کی بیع سلم میں دیا یعنی نقو تو نقد ادا کر دیا گیا اور مسلم فیہ یعنی زعفران یا روئی وغیرہ کو ایک میعاد معلوم تک کیلئے ادھار کر دیا گیا تو یہ جائز ہے اگر چہ نقود اور زعفران دونوں وزنی ہیں یعنی نقود اور زعفران میں احد الوصفین یعنی قدر موجود ہونے کا تقاضہ تو یہ تھا کہ نسا ء حرام ہو لیکن اس کے باوجود نساء حرام نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ نقو داور زعفران اگر چہ دونوں وزنی ہیں لیکن وزن کی صفت اور وزن کے معنی اور وزن کے حکم میں دونوں مختلف ہیں وزن کی صفت میں اختلاف اس لیے ہے کہ زعفران کو من اور سیر سے تولا جاتا ہے اور نقود کو سنگ تر از ولیعنی مشائیل اور دراہم سے تو لا جاتا ہے یہ خیال رہے کہ یہاں من اور سیر سے مراد آج کل کا من اور سیر مراد نہیں بلکہ یہ من بہت چھوٹا اور کم وزن کا ہوتا تھا اورقو د اور زعفران دونوں کے وزن میں معنی اختلاف اس لئے ہے کہ نقود متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتے اور وہ شمن ہوتے ہیں اور زعفران مثمن ہوتی ہے متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتی ہے اور وزن کے حکم میں اختلاف اس لئے ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نقود کے عوض وزن کے حساب سے زعفران فروخت کی مثلاً خالد نے ایک من زعفران ایک ہزار مثقال سونے کے وزن کے برابر کے عوض حامد کو فروخت کی یعنی خالد نے ایک من زعفران فروخت کی اور ایک ہزار مثقال سونا ثمن قرار دیا پس بائع نے مشتری کی عدم موجودگی میں زعفران وزن کر کے مشتری کے سپرد کر دی تو مشتری کے لئے اعادہ وزن سے پہلے اس میں تصرف کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اور جب
Chapter of Sales. Imam Shafi'i completely denies the prohibition of nasi'ah (credit), whether the genus (jins) exists or the measure (qadr) exists. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 8. The response to this is that selling gold for silver on credit and wheat for barley on credit is not prohibited because in their view nasi'ah is forbidden, but rather because in their view in bay' al-sarf (money exchange) and bay' al-ta'am (food exchange), mutual possession within the session is a condition. Selling gold for silver is bay' al-sarf, and selling wheat for barley is bay' al-ta'am. Mutual possession within the session is only possible when the sale is not on credit but spot. It is clear that mutual possession within the session is also necessary in our view in bay' al-sarf. In any case, the conclusion is that mere genus or mere measure does not make credit prohibited in the view of Imam Shafi'i. This is supported by a hadith from Ibn Umar: that the Messenger of Allah prepared an army and ordered me to buy a camel on credit (as salam) for two camels. And in another narration, that Ali sold a camel for two camels on credit (Fath al-Qadir). These narrations also prove that mere existence of genus does not make nasi'ah prohibited. Our evidence is that in the chapter of riba, there is a reality of riba (haqiqat al-riba) and a semblance of riba (shubhat al-riba). When the semblance of riba is found separate from the reality of riba, it requires a different locus and a different cause, just as the reality of riba requires both. It is not possible that the locus and cause of shubhat al-riba be the same as those of haqiqat al-riba, because if so, it would not remain shubhat al-riba but become haqiqat al-riba, contrary to assumption. Therefore, for shubhat al-riba, a semblance of locus and a semblance of cause are necessary. And the sale in which nasi'ah is prohibited has exchange items that are from the perspective of ribawi wealth, because either there is unity of measure (as in selling wheat for barley) or unity of genus (as in selling Herat cloth for Herat cloth). It is established that the effective cause of riba consists of two attributes: measure and genus. Therefore, one of them cannot be the cause of riba. It can, however, be a semblance of cause (shubhat al-'illah). From the semblance of cause, a semblance of the ruling (shubhat al-hukm, i.e., shubhat al-riba) is established, not the reality of riba. So when one exchange is spot and the other is credit, the spot nature creates an increase in value, as is clear from the saying 'al-naqd khayrun min al-nasi'ah' (cash is better than credit). Thus, the spot nature creates a semblance of riba in that locus, and shubhat al-riba prevents the permissibility of the sale just as haqiqat al-riba prevents it, because the Messenger of Allah prohibited both riba and its semblance. So it is established that the existence of one of the two attributes (measure or genus) makes nasi'ah prohibited. Due to this shubhat al-riba, it is not permissible to sell ribawi goods by estimation. For example, if a person sells one heap of wheat for another heap of wheat by estimation, even if the two heaps appear equal, it is not permissible because of the semblance of increase. This also shows that shubhat al-riba prevents the permissibility of the sale. In fact, except for Imam Zufar, the Hanafi jurists have said that if one heap of wheat is sold for another heap by estimation, then both heaps are measured and turn out equal, still it is not permissible in our view. The prohibition of nasi'ah when one of the two attributes exists is also deduced from hadith. Thus, the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn Samit at the end of the riba hadith: 'When these categories differ, then sell as you wish provided it is hand-to-hand.' Observe: In this hadith, when the genus differs, permission to sell with increase or decrease is given, but making mutual possession necessary is itself the prohibition of nasi'ah. That is, when possession becomes necessary for the two exchange items, nasi'ah becomes prohibited. So it is established that when one of the two attributes (i.e., measure) exists, nasi'ah is prohibited. And in Abu Dawud's narration: 'There is no harm in selling wheat for barley even if barley is more, hand-to-hand, but as for credit, it is not permissible.' From this narration, it is understood that if measure exists but genus does not, nasi'ah is prohibited. Also, in Abu Dawud, from Samurah: 'The Prophet prohibited selling animals for animals on credit.' This narration shows that when genus exists but measure does not, nasi'ah is also prohibited. The response to the hadith presented by Imam Shafi'i: The response to the hadith of Ibn Umar and the hadith of 'Ali is that the narrations of Ibn Umar and 'Ali permit nasi'ah even when one attribute (i.e., genus) exists, while the narrations we presented prohibit nasi'ah. The principle is that when there is conflict between what prohibits and what permits, the prohibiting takes precedence. Therefore, our narrations are preponderant. The second response is that the hadith of Ibn Umar and the hadith of 'Ali are from before the prohibition of riba, and the narrations we cited are from after the prohibition of riba. With this response, no conflict remains. The statement of the author of Hidayah: 'Except when one advances money (nuqud) for saffron' — the phrase of the author of Hidayah is an exception to the previous statement: 'When one of the two exists and the other is absent, then disparity (tafadul) is permissible but nasi'ah is prohibited.' But one case is excepted from this: if money (gold or silver) is given in a salam sale for saffron or similar items like cotton, iron, etc., meaning the price is paid spot and the subject matter (saffron or cotton) is left as credit for a known term, then it is permissible even though both money and saffron are weight-based items. That is, the requirement that when one attribute (measure) exists, nasi'ah should be prohibited, but despite that, nasi'ah is not prohibited here. Because although money and saffron are both weight-based, they differ in the quality of weight, the meaning of weight, and the ruling of weight. They differ in the quality of weight because saffron is weighed by the mann and seer, while money is weighed by the stone-weight (sang-e-tarazu) i.e., mithqal and dirhams. Note that here mann and seer do not refer to the current mann and seer; rather, this mann was very small and light. The difference in meaning of weight is that money is not determined by specification; it is a price (thaman), while saffron is a commodity (muthman) and is determined by specification. The difference in the ruling of weight is that if someone sells saffron by weight in exchange for money, e.g., Khalid sold one mann of saffron to Hamid for the equivalent weight of one thousand mithqals of gold, i.e., Khalid sold one mann of saffron and set one thousand mithqals of gold as the price, then if the seller weighs the saffron and hands it over to the buyer in the buyer's absence, the buyer is not permitted to dispose of it before re-weighing. And when...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, deals with the prohibition of nasi'ah (credit/deferred payment) in sales of ribawi items. The discussion is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. The specific issue: Does the existence of either genus (jins) or measure (qadr) alone in a ribawi exchange make credit prohibited? Imam al-Shafi'i holds that credit is prohibited only when BOTH genus and measure are present (i.e., when the exchange is of the same genus and same measure, like wheat for wheat) OR when it involves a sale where hand-to-hand possession is required by consensus (like bay' al-sarf). He denies that the mere presence of genus (e.g., selling an animal for an animal of different type) or mere presence of measure (e.g., selling wheat for barley) prohibits credit. He cites the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ali allowing credit when genus alone exists. The Hanafi response: The prohibition of credit is based on shubhat al-riba (semblance of riba), not haqiqat al-riba (actual riba). Riba's cause (illah) is the combination of genus and measure. When only one attribute exists, it is not the actual cause, but it creates a semblance of the cause (shubhat al-'illah), which leads to shubhat al-hukm (shubhat al-riba). This semblance is enough to prohibit credit because the Prophet prohibited both riba and its semblance. The Hanafis then provide hadith evidence: the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn Samit shows that when genus differs, hand-to-hand possession is required, implying credit is prohibited. The hadith of Abu Dawud shows that when measure exists but genus differs (wheat for barley), credit is prohibited. The hadith of Samurah shows that when genus exists but measure does not (animals), credit is also prohibited. In response to Shafi'i's hadith, the Hanafis give two answers: (1) Prohibiting takes precedence over permitting when texts conflict. (2) The hadiths of Ibn Umar and Ali are abrogated (mansukh) because they occurred before the prohibition of riba, while the Hanafi proof-texts are later. Finally, an exception is noted from the author of Hidayah: In a salam sale where the price (nuqud) is paid spot and the subject matter (like saffron) is deferred, credit is permissible despite both items being weight-based. The reasoning is that although both are weighed, they differ in the quality, meaning, and ruling of weight. For example, money is not determined by specification (it is a price), while saffron is determined by specification (it is a commodity). Additionally, the weight units differ (mann/seer vs. mithqal/dirham). This makes the case distinct from the general rule.

Key Terms
نساء (نسیئہ) (nasā' / nasi'ah): Credit sale; deferred payment in a sale where possession of one or both exchanges is postponed.
شبہۃ الربوا (shubhat al-ribā): A semblance or apparent resemblance to riba, which carries the same legal ruling as actual riba in terms of prohibition.
أحد الوصفین (aḥad al-waṣfayn): One of the two attributes (jins or qadr) that constitute the effective cause of riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on selling wheat for barley on credit (nasi'ah)?
A) Permissible because the genera are different
B) Prohibited because measure (qadr) exists in both, creating shubhat al-riba
C) Permissible only if the quantities are equal
D) Prohibited only if both are sold by weight

Key Takeaway
Nasi'ah is prohibited when either genus or measure exists due to shubhat al-riba, based on hadith and the principle of blocking the means to riba.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i: The Ruling on Nasi'ah When One Characteristic Is Present
Hanafi refutation of Shafi'i's hadith permitting nasi'ah when one characteristic is present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that nasi'ah is prohibited when either jins or qadr is present, and explain the two Hanafi responses to the Shafi'i counter-evidence.

Core Idea
Nasi'ah is prohibited when either jins or qadr is present; a prohibitor outweighs a permitter.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: when two ribawi items differ in genus but share a common measure (qadr), or share a genus but differ in measure, is credit (nasi'ah) allowed? The Hanafi school holds that credit is prohibited based on specific hadith, while Imam al-Shafi'i cites other hadith permitting it. The author provides two powerful Hanafi responses that resolve the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: nasi'ah is prohibited whenever either jins (same genus) or qadr (quantity measure) is present in a ribawi exchange, even if the other characteristic is absent.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that nasi'ah is permissible when only one characteristic (jins or qadr) is present, citing hadith from Ibn 'Umar and 'Ali.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith that Shafi'i uses: they apparently permit credit sales despite the presence of one characteristic.
These hadith are the basis of the Shafi'i position.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Two responses: (1) Legal principle: when a prohibitor and permitter conflict, the prohibitor is given preference. (2) Abrogation: the Shafi'i hadith are from before the final prohibition of riba, while the Hanafi proofs are after.
The second response removes any genuine conflict.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis deem such credit transactions haram; Shafi'is permit them. This affects everyday commodity exchanges.

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The author begins by establishing the Hanafi position: when two items of different species are exchanged, if one of the two characteristics (jins or qadr) is present, nasi'ah (credit) is prohibited. He cites two hadith from Abu Dawud as proof: the first shows that when qadr is present but jins is absent, credit is prohibited; the second shows that when jins is present but qadr is absent, credit is also prohibited. Shafi'i countered with hadith from Ibn 'Umar and 'Ali that apparently permit nasi'ah. The author gives two Hanafi responses: first, by legal principle, when a prohibitor and a permitter conflict, the prohibitor is given preference; second, the Shafi'i hadith are from before the definitive prohibition of riba, whereas the Hanafi proofs are later, making them abrogating. Thus the Hanafi view is stronger.

Key Terms
نسیئہ (nasi'ah): Credit sale where delivery of one or both items is deferred
تفاضل (tafaddul): Excess in quantity or value between two exchanged items

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible because they are different species
B) Prohibited because nasi'ah is haram when qadr is present
C) Permissible only if hand-to-hand
D) Prohibited only if both are measured

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, nasi'ah in ribawi items is prohibited when either jins or qadr is present, based on the principle of preference for prohibitors and abrogation.

Exception to the Rule: Salam in Cash for Saffron
Exception to the rule that credit on weighed items is haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a salam contract for saffron with cash is permissible despite both being weighed, and apply the principle of shubhat al-shubhah to similar cases.

Core Idea
A doubt of a doubt is no doubt at all — so the salam contract is valid.

In this lesson, we explore an exception to the general rule that credit sales of two weighed items are prohibited. The Hidayah had stated that when one characteristic (qadr) is present, nasi'ah is haram. However, the commentator carves out an exception for salam with cash and saffron, using the subtle legal concept of shubhat al-shubhah. Understanding this exception requires careful attention to the three dimensions of weight: nature, meaning, and ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
Recall the principle from earlier: if two items share one characteristic (qadr or jins) but differ in the other, tafaddul is halal and nasi'ah is haram. Note that the commentator states an exception: salam where cash is paid for saffron is permissible despite both being weighed.
The exception is only for salam contracts where cash is paid immediately.
2
Recognize the three differences in weight characteristics
The passage lists three ways in which cash and saffron differ: in the nature of their weight units (mann/seer vs. mithqal/dirham), in the meaning (cash is thaman, saffron is mithman), and in the ruling on disposal after weighing (buyer may not dispose of saffron without reweighing, but seller may dispose of cash immediately).
These differences prevent complete unity of measurement.
3
Trace how these differences lead to shubhat al-shubhah
Because the two items do not agree in weight from every aspect, the doubt (shubhah) of riba that would arise from similarity is only a doubt of a doubt. Earlier it was established that if weighed items are identical in weight but different in species, nasi'ah is haram due to a direct doubt of riba. Here, since they differ in weight characteristics, the doubt is weakened to shubhat al-shubhah.
Shubhat al-shubhah is not legally significant.
4
Conclude why the exception is valid
In Hanafi law, a direct doubt (shubhah) is considered, but a doubt of a doubt (shubhat al-shubhah) is ignored. Therefore, the credit element in this salam contract is not prohibited, and the contract is permissible.
This ruling is specific to salam where cash is the price.

کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے اور جب مشتری نے بائع کی عدم موجودگی میں نقو دوزن کر کے بائع کے سپر د کر دیئے تو دوبارہ وزن کرنے سے پہلے بائع کے لیے نقود میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے تصرف کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بائع ان نقود کے عوض کوئی دوسری چیز خرید سکتا ہے ان کو ہبہ اور صدقہ بھی کر سکتا ہے پس جب نقود اور زعفران وزن میں صورت معنی اور حکم کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہیں تو ان دونوں میں اتحاد قدر من کل وجہ نہیں پایا گیا اور جب اتحاد قد رمن کل وجہ نہیں پایا گیا تو اس میں شہبتہ الر بواشبہ الشبہ کے درجہ میں ہو جائے گا کیونکہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ دو موزونی چیزیں اگر من کل وجہ وزن میں متفق ہوں اور دونوں کی جنس ایک نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں نساء ( ادھار ) شنبہ رہا کیوجہ سے حرام ہوتا ہے اور جب دونوں وزن میں بھی متفق نہ ہوں تو یہ شبہ وزن ہوگا پس جب تنبا وزن کی وجہ سے شہبتہ الر ہوا پیدا ہوتا ہے تو شبہ وزن کی وجہ سے شہبتہ الشبہ پیدا ہو گا یعنی شبہ وزن کی وجہ سے ربوا کے شبہ کا شبہ پیدا ہوگا اور شریعت اسلام میں شبہ تو معتبر ہے لیکن شبتہ الشبہ معتبر نہیں ہے اس لیے نقود کے عوض زعفران کی بیع سلم یعنی ادھار جائز ہے۔
The statement of the author of al-Hidayah: 'Except when one pays cash for saffron...' The expression of the author of al-Hidayah is an exception from [the rule] 'So when one of them is present and the other is absent, excess is halal and nasi'ah is haram.' So previously it was stated that if one of the two characteristics, qadr or jins, is present and the other is absent, then excess is halal and nasi'ah is haram. But one case is exempt from this: if cash, i.e., gold or silver, is given in a salam contract for saffron or similar things like cotton, iron, etc., meaning that the cash is paid immediately, and the subject of the salam, i.e., saffron or cotton, is deferred to a known term, then this is permissible even though both cash and saffron are weighed. That is, the requirement for cash and saffron due to the presence of one characteristic, i.e., qadr, would have been that nasi'ah is haram, but despite this, nasi'ah is not haram. Because cash and saffron, although both are weighed, differ in the nature of weight, the meaning of weight, and the ruling of weight. The difference in the nature of weight is that saffron is weighed in mann and seer, while cash is weighed in mithqal and dirhams. Note that mann and seer here do not refer to modern units but were very small and light. The difference in the meaning of weight is that cash, when specified, does not become determined (it remains a price), while saffron is a commodity that becomes determined by specification. The difference in the ruling of weight is that if someone sells saffron by weight for cash, e.g., Khalid sold one mann of saffron to Hamid for the weight equivalent of one thousand mithqals of gold, then if the seller weighs and delivers the saffron in the absence of the buyer, the buyer may not dispose of it without reweighing; but if the buyer weighs and delivers the cash in the absence of the seller, the seller may dispose of the cash immediately without reweighing. Since cash and saffron differ in the nature, meaning, and ruling of weight, complete unity of measurement from every aspect is not found. And when complete unity of measurement is not found, it becomes a case of shubhat al-riba (doubt of riba) at the level of shubhat al-shubhah (doubt of doubt). Earlier it was established that if two weighed items agree in weight from every aspect and their species differ, then nasi'ah is haram due to the doubt of riba. But when they do not agree in weight, it is a doubt of weight. So when the doubt of weight creates shubhat al-riba, then the doubt of weight creates shubhat al-shubhah, i.e., a doubt of the doubt of riba. And in Islamic law, a doubt is considered, but a doubt of a doubt is not considered. Therefore, a salam sale of saffron for cash on credit is permissible.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on a specific exception from the general riba rules. The author of al-Hidayah had stated that when one of the two characteristics (jins or qadr) is present, tafaddul is halal and nasi'ah is haram. However, there is an exception: if one pays cash (gold or silver) immediately in a salam contract for a weighed commodity like saffron (or cotton, iron, etc.), it is permissible even though both are weighed. The reason is that although both are weighed, they differ in three aspects: the nature of their weight units, the meaning (cash is thaman, saffron is mithman), and the ruling on disposition after weighing. Hence there is no complete unity of measurement. The commentary explains that if two weighed items are completely identical in weight characteristics but of different species, nasi'ah is haram due to shubhat al-riba. Here, since they differ in weight characteristics, there is only shubhat al-shubhah (doubt of doubt), which is not legally effective. Therefore, the salam contract is valid.

Key Terms
قدر (qadr): Measurement; one of the two characteristics (along with jins) that determine riba applicability.
جنس (jins): Type or species; the other characteristic alongside qadr.
شبهة الربوا (shubhat al-riba): Doubt of usury; a level of uncertainty that legally affects the ruling.
سلم (salam): A sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later
شبهة الشبہ (shubhat al-shubhah): Doubt of a doubt; a level of uncertainty that is not considered legally relevant

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a salam contract for saffron with gold permissible despite both being weighed items?
A) Because they are of different species
B) Because the weight units are the same
C) Because they differ in the nature, meaning, and ruling of weight
D) Because such transactions are always permissible

Key Takeaway
A salam contract for a weighed commodity with cash is permissible because the difference in weight characteristics reduces the doubt to an ineffective level.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Permanence of Measure/Weight Classification from Revelation
Ruling from al-Quduri's matn on permanent classification of makil/mawzun

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that items designated by the Prophet as measured or weighed remain in that category forever, and apply it to determine the validity of a sale of like items.

Core Idea
The Prophet's designation of measured/weighed items is permanent – text overrides custom.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes a foundational maxim in Hanafi fiqh of transactions: items explicitly classified by the Prophet as measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) retain that classification permanently, regardless of changes in people's customs. This principle has direct implications for riba: when exchanging like-for-like, equality must be achieved according to the original classification. The commentary provides two proofs: the obligation of obedience and the superiority of text over custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that items designated by the Prophet as makil or mawzun remain in that status forever, even if people change their measurement practices.
This is a general principle (qa'ida).
2
Identify the examples
Makil items include wheat, barley, dates, and salt. Mawzun items include gold and silver.
These are examples; the principle applies to all such items specified in the hadith.
3
Understand the proofs
Two proofs: (1) obedience to the Prophet is wajib, so his designation binds us; (2) text (nass) is stronger than custom, because custom can be based on falsehood.
The commentary emphasizes that nass cannot be abandoned for a weaker basis like custom.
4
Apply the ruling
For example, if wheat (makil) is sold for wheat, equality must be achieved by volume; using weight makes the sale invalid due to riba.
The same applies to gold: equality must be by weight, not volume.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may hold that if custom changes entirely, the classification can shift. The Hanafi school insists on permanence based on the strength of the text.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وكل شيء نص رسول الله عليه السلام على تحريم التفاضل فيه مكيلا فهو مكيل ابداوان ترک الناس الكيل فيه مثل الحنطة والشعير و التمرو الملح وكل مانص على تحريم التفاضل فيه وزنا فهو موزون ابدا وان ترك الناس الوزن فيه مثل الذهب والفضة لان النص اقوى من العرف والاقوى لا يترك بالادنى ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جن چیزوں میں کیل کی راہ سے زیادتی حرام ہونے کی تصریح فرمائی ہے وہ ہمیشہ کیلی رہیں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے ان میں کیل کرنا چھوڑ دیا وہ جیسے گندم، جو، چھوہارے، نمک اور جس چیز میں رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وزن کے اعتبار سے زیادتی حرام ہونے کی تصریح فرمائی ہے وہ ہمیشہ وزنی رہیں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے اس میں وزن کرنا چھوڑ دیا ہو جیسے سونا اور چاندی ۔ کیونکہ نص، به نسبت رواج اور عرف کے زیادہ قوی ہوتی ہے اور اقوی کو ادنی کی وجہ سے نہیں چھوڑا جائے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عہد رسالت میں جو چیز کیلی تھی یعنی آپ اور آپ کے صحابہ اس میں کیل سے معاملہ کرتے تھے وہ ہمیشہ کیلی شمار ہوں گی اگر چہ لوگوں نے اس میں کیل کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنا ترک کر دیا ہو جیسے گندم، جو، چھوہارے اور نمک پس ان چیزوں میں مساوات اور برابری کیل کے ذریعہ معتبر ہوگی نہ کہ وزن کے ذریعہ چنا نچہ اگر گندم کو گندم کے عوض بیچا گیا اور برابری وزن کے ذریعہ کی گئی نہ کہ کیل کے ذریعہ تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ گندم عہد رسالت میں کیلی تھی اس لیے اس میں قیامت تک کیل ہی کے ذریعہ مساوات اور برابری معتبر ہوگی وزن کے ذریعہ معتبر نہ ہوگی ۔ اور جو چیز عہد رسالت میں وزنی تھی یعنی لوگ اس میں وزن کے ساتھ معاملہ کرتے تھے تو وہ ہمیشہ وزنی شمار ہوگی اگر چہ اس میں لوگوں نے وزن کے ساتھ معاملہ کرنا ترک کر دیا ہو جیسے سونا اور چاندی حتی کہ اگر سونا سونے کے عوض بیچا گیا اور کیل کے ذریعہ برابری کی گئی نہ کہ وزن کے ذریعہ تو یہ جائز نہ ہوگا اس کی ایک دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی اطاعت ہم پر واجب ہے پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جس کو کیلی قرار دیا وہ ہمیشہ کیلی شمار ہوگی اور جس کو وزنی قرار دیا وہ ہمیشہ وزنی شمار ہوگی ۔ اگر چہ لوگوں کا معاملہ اس کے خلاف پر ہو۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نص یعنی حدیث رسول عرف اور رواج کی بہ نسبت اقومی ہے کیونکہ عرف تو باطل پر بھی ہو سکتا ہے جیسا کہ صاحب فتح القدیر کے زمانہ میں عید کی رات میں قبرستان میں چراغان کرنے پر عرف تھا اور جیسا کہ ہمارے زمانے میں آم ظاہر ہونے
He said: And every item for which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) explicitly stated that excess is prohibited while it is measured (makil) – it remains measured forever, even if people abandon measurement in it, like wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And every item for which he explicitly stated that excess is prohibited while it is weighed (mawzun) – it remains weighed forever, even if people abandon weighing in it, like gold and silver. Because the text (nass) is stronger than custom, and the stronger is not abandoned for the weaker. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the items regarding which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) explicitly stated that excess is prohibited through measurement will always be measured, even if people abandon measuring them, such as wheat, barley, dates, and salt. And the items regarding which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) explicitly stated that excess is prohibited through weight will always be weighed, even if people abandon weighing them, such as gold and silver. Because the text is stronger than custom and practice, and the stronger is not left for the weaker. Explanation: The issue is that whatever was measured in the era of the Prophet – i.e., he and his Companions dealt with it by measure – will always be considered measured, even if people have abandoned measuring it, like wheat, barley, dates, and salt. Therefore, in these items, equality and equivalence will be by measure, not by weight. So if wheat is sold for wheat and equality is achieved by weight instead of measure, it is not permissible, because wheat was measured in the Prophet's era, so until the Day of Judgment, equality will be by measure, not by weight. And whatever was weighed in the Prophet's era – i.e., people dealt with it by weight – will always be considered weighed, even if people have abandoned weighing it, like gold and silver. Even if gold is sold for gold and equality is achieved by measure instead of weight, it is not permissible. One proof is that obedience to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) is obligatory upon us; so whatever he designated as measured will always be measured, and whatever he designated as weighed will always be weighed, even if people's practice is contrary. The second proof is that the text (hadith) is stronger than custom and practice, because custom can be based on falsehood, such as the custom in the time of the author of Fath al-Qadir of lighting lamps in the graveyard on the night of Eid, and like in our time, mangoes appearing
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting a foundational qa'ida (maxim) from al-Quduri's matn. The text establishes that items explicitly designated by the Prophet as measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun) remain in that category perpetually, even if people change their customs. The examples: wheat, barley, dates, and salt are permanently measured; gold and silver are permanently weighed. The commentary provides two proofs: first, the obligation of obedience to the Prophet's designation, which overrides subsequent custom; second, the principle that textual evidence (nass) is stronger than custom, because custom may be based on false or changing practices. The passage also gives a negative application: if wheat is sold for wheat with equality by weight, it is invalid; similarly, gold sold for gold with equality by measure is invalid. The commentary ends with an example of a false custom (lighting lamps in graveyards on Eid night) to illustrate that custom is not a valid basis for overriding nass.

Key Terms
کیلی (makil): An item that was measured by volume in the Prophet's era and remains legally so forever.
وزنی (mawzun): An item that was weighed in the Prophet's era and remains legally so forever.
نص (nass): Textual evidence from the Quran or Hadith that is clear and definitive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person sells wheat (a makil item) for wheat and achieves equality by weight instead of volume, what is the ruling?
A) Permissible because equality is achieved
B) Impermissible because the measure of equality must be by volume as per the Prophet's designation
C) Permissible if both parties agree
D) Impermissible only if there is excess

Key Takeaway
Items explicitly measured or weighed by the Prophet remain in that category forever; text overrides custom.
